29958222|ab|1|29958222|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|OBJECTIVE|The aepEXplus monitoring system, which uses mid-latency auditory evoked potentials to measure depth of hypnosis, was evaluated in pediatric patients receiving desflurane-remifentanil anesthesia.
29958222|ab|2|29958222|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|Seventy-five patients, 1-18 years of age (stratified for age; 1-3, 3-6, 6-18 years, for subgroup analyses), were included in this prospective observational study.
29958222|ab|3|29958222|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|The aepEX and the bispectral index (BIS) were recorded simultaneously, the latter serving as a reference.
29958222|ab|4|29958222|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|The ability of the aepEX to detect different levels of consciousness, defined according to the University of Michigan Sedation Scale, investigated using prediction probability (Pk), and receiver operating characteristic (ROC) analysis, served as the primary outcome parameter.
29958222|ab|5|29958222|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|As a secondary outcome parameter, the relationship between end-tidal desflurane and the aepEX and BIS values were calculated by fitting in a nonlinear regression model.
29958222|ab|6|29958222|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|The Pk values for the aepEX and the BIS were, respectively, .68 (95% CI, 0.53-0.82) and .85 (95% CI, 0.73-0.96; P = .02).
29958222|ab|7|29958222|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|The aepEX and the BIS had an area under the ROC curve of, respectively, 0.89 (95% CI, 0.80-0.95) and 0.76 (95% CI, 0.68-0.84; P = .04).
29958222|ab|8|29958222|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|The maximized sensitivity and specificity were, respectively, 81% (95% CI, 61%-93%) and 86% (95% CI, 74%-94%) for the aepEX at a cutoff value of >52, and 69% (95% CI, 56%-81%) and 70% (95% CI, 57%-81%) for the BIS at a cutoff value of >65.
29958222|ab|9|29958222|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|The age-corrected end-tidal desflurane concentration associated with an index value of 50 (EC50) was 0.59 minimum alveolar concentration (interquartile range: 0.38-0.85) and 0.58 minimum alveolar concentration (interquartile range: 0.41-0.70) for, respectively, the aepEX and BIS (P = .69).
29958222|ab|10|29958222|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Age-group analysis showed no evidence of a difference regarding the area under the ROC curve or EC50.
29958222|ab|11|29958222|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|The aepEX can reliably differentiate between a conscious and an unconscious state in pediatric patients receiving desflurane-remifentanil anesthesia.
29950143|ab|1|29950143|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|Bone-regulating hormones and nutrients play an important role in influencing metabolic health.
29950143|ab|2|29950143|AIM|OBJECTIVE|OBJECTIVE|The aim of this study was to determine whether bone-regulating hormones and nutrients, such as parathyroid hormone (PTH), 25-hydroxyvitamin D (25OHD), and magnesium (Mg) could be used to characterize the metabolically healthy obese (MHO) phenotype.
29950143|ab|3|29950143|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|This study included 27 overweight or obese participants (14 men/13 women) classified as MHO ( n = 14) or metabolically unhealthy obese (MUO) ( n = 13) based on the presence or absence of metabolic abnormalities, determined by percentage body fat, percentage trunk fat, and waist circumference.
29950143|ab|4|29950143|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|Biochemical (serum concentrations of hormones and cytokines such as PTH, 25OHD, ionized Mg (iMg), cytokines, lipids, glycemic indices), physiological (percentage body fat, percentage trunk fat, blood pressure (BP)), and dietary intake (Mg intake, calcium intake) measurements were obtained.
29950143|ab|5|29950143|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Serum PTH concentrations were significantly lower ( p = 0.005) in the MHO group (39.68 +/- 11.06 pg/mL) compared with the MUO group (63.78 +/- 25.82 pg/mL).
29950143|ab|6|29950143|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Serum iMg concentrations were higher ( p = 0.052) in the MHO group (0.565 +/- 0.41 mmol/L) than in the MUO group (0.528 +/- 0.050 mmol/L).
29950143|ab|7|29950143|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Serum concentrations of osteocalcin were also higher (10.37 +/- 3.70 ng/mL) in the MHO compared with the MUO (6.51 +/- 4.14 ng/mL) group ( p = 0.017).
29950143|ab|8|29950143|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|The MHO group had significantly lower serum insulin concentrations ( p = 0.006) and diastolic BP ( p = 0.035).
29950143|ab|9|29950143|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Concentrations of serum 25OHD, total triglycerides, C-reactive protein and systolic BP did not differ between groups.
29950143|ab|10|29950143|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|These findings suggest that bone-regulating hormones and nutrients, especially serum PTH, osteocalcin concentrations, and dietary Mg intakes, can help to characterize the MHO phenotype.
29949784|ab|1|29949784|BACKGROUND/AIMS|OBJECTIVE|BACKGROUND|Gastric cancer (GC) is one of the most prevalent digestive malignancies.
29949784|ab|2|29949784|BACKGROUND/AIMS|OBJECTIVE|BACKGROUND|MicroRNAs (miRNAs) are involved in multiple cellular processes, including oncogenesis, and miR-592 itself participates in many malignancies; however, its role in GC remains unknown.
29949784|ab|3|29949784|BACKGROUND/AIMS|OBJECTIVE|OBJECTIVE|In this study, we investigated the expression and molecular mechanisms of miR-592 in GC.
29949784|ab|4|29949784|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|Quantitative real-time PCR and immunohistochemistry were performed to determine the expression of miR-592 and its putative targets in human tissues and cell lines.
29949784|ab|5|29949784|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|Proliferation, migration, and invasion were evaluated by Cell Counting Kit-8, population doubling time, colony formation, Transwell, and wound-healing assays in transfected GC cells in vitro.
29949784|ab|6|29949784|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|A dual-luciferase reporter assay was used to determine whether miR-592 could directly bind its target.
29949784|ab|7|29949784|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|A tumorigenesis assay was used to study whether miR-592 affected GC growth in vivo.
29949784|ab|8|29949784|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|Proteins involved in signaling pathways and the epithelial-mesenchymal transition (EMT) were detected with western blot.
29949784|ab|9|29949784|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|The ectopic expression of miR-592 promoted GC proliferation, migration, and invasion in vitro and facilitated tumorigenesis in vivo.
29949784|ab|10|29949784|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Spry2 was a direct target of miR-592 and Spry2 overexpression partially counteracted the effects of miR-592.
29949784|ab|11|29949784|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|miR-592 induced the EMT and promoted its progression in GC via the PI3K/AKT and MAPK/ERK signaling pathways by inhibiting Spry2.
29949784|ab|12|29949784|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|Overexpression of miR-592 promotes GC proliferation, migration, and invasion and induces the EMT via the PI3K/AKT and MAPK/ERK signaling pathways by inhibiting Spry2, suggesting a potential therapeutic target for GC.
20211270|ab|1|20211270||BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|Regularity of laminar origin and termination of projections appears to be a common feature of corticocortical connections.
20211270|ab|2|20211270||BACKGROUND|OBJECTIVE|We tested three models of this regularity, originally formulated for primate cerebral cortex, using quantitative data on the relative supragranular layer origins (SGN%) of 151 projections from 19 areas ( approximately 145,000 neurons) to four areas of cat extrastriate cortex.
20211270|ab|3|20211270||METHODS|METHODS|Predictive variables in the models were: hierarchical level differences (Barone et al., 2000), structural type differences (Barbas, 1986), and distances (Salin and Bullier, 1995) between areas.
20211270|ab|4|20211270||METHODS|METHODS|Global and local hierarchies of cat visual cortex were used to evaluate the hierarchical model.
20211270|ab|5|20211270||METHODS|METHODS|Ranking of areas by their cytoarchitectural differentiation (e.g., relative prominence of layer IV) allowed testing of the structural model, while the distance model was tested for the number of borders separating areas.
20211270|ab|6|20211270||RESULTS|RESULTS|Laminar projection origins correlated moderately with hierarchical differences, and poorly with border distances, but were strongly and consistently correlated with area differences in cytoarchitectural rank.
20211270|ab|7|20211270||RESULTS|RESULTS|Moreover, projection densities were moderately and negatively correlated with area distances and structural differences.
20211270|ab|8|20211270||CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|Our findings suggest that the relative cytoarchitectural differentiation of cortical areas is the main determinant of laminar projection origins in cat visual cortex, and may underlie a general laminar regularity of mammalian cortical connections.
29954372|ab|1|29954372|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|Despite the growing interest in developing markers for predicting treatment response and optimizing treatment decisions, an appropriate methodology to identify, combine and evaluate such markers has been slow to develop.
29954372|ab|2|29954372|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|OBJECTIVE|We propose a step-by-step strategy for analysing data from existing randomised trials with the aim of identifying a multi-marker model for guiding decisions about treatment.
29954372|ab|3|29954372|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|We start with formulating the treatment selection problem, continue with defining the treatment threshold, prepare a list of candidate markers, develop the model, apply the model to estimate individual treatment effects, and evaluate model performance in the study group of patients who meet the trial eligibility criteria.
29954372|ab|4|29954372|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|In this process, we rely on some well-known techniques for multivariable prediction modelling, but focus on predicting benefit from treatment, rather than outcome itself.
29954372|ab|5|29954372|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|We present our approach using data from a randomised trial in which 808 women with multiple pregnancy were assigned to cervical pessary or control, to prevent adverse perinatal outcomes.
29954372|ab|6|29954372|METHODS|METHODS|RESULTS|Overall, cervical pessary did not reduce the risk of adverse perinatal outcomes.
29954372|ab|7|29954372|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|The treatment threshold was zero.
29954372|ab|8|29954372|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|We had a preselected list of 5 potential markers and developed a logistic model including the markers, treatment and all marker-by-treatment interaction terms.
29954372|ab|9|29954372|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|The model was well calibrated and identified 35% (95% confidence interval (CI) 32 to 39%) of the trial participants as benefitting from pessary insertion.
29954372|ab|10|29954372|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|We estimated that the risk of adverse outcome could be reduced from 13.5 to 8.1% (5.4% risk reduction; 95% CI 2.1 to 8.6%) through model-based selective pessary insertion.
29954372|ab|11|29954372|RESULTS|RESULTS|CONCLUSIONS|The next step is external validation upon existence of independent trial data.
29954372|ab|12|29954372|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|We suggest revisiting existing trials data to explore whether differences in treatment benefit can be explained by differences in baseline characteristics of patients.
29954372|ab|13|29954372|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|This could lead to treatment selection tools which, after validation in comparable existing trials, can be introduced into clinical practice for guiding treatment decisions in future patients.
18657335|ab|1|18657335||BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|Diabetes mellitus is the most common chronic metabolic disease.
18657335|ab|2|18657335||BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|The raising diabetes epidemic is unfolding as an interaction between several environmental factors and a genetic predisposition.
18657335|ab|3|18657335||OBJECTIVE|OBJECTIVE|The aim of the current study was to evaluate the role of the PPARgamma-Pro12Ala and ENPP1-K121Q polymorphisms on type 2 diabetes (T2D) risk in a case-control study in the Tunisian population.
18657335|ab|4|18657335||METHODS|METHODS|To assess for any association of ENPP1-K121Q and PPARgamma-Pro12Ala polymorphisms with T2D risk, we analysed the genotypic and allelic distributions of each variant in the studied cohort.
18657335|ab|5|18657335||RESULTS|RESULTS|Our results support that the genetic variation at ENPP1-K121Q predisposes to T2D in the Tunisian population after adjustment on gender, age and BMI status (OR=1.55, 95%CI [1.11-2.16], p=0.007).
18657335|ab|6|18657335||RESULTS|RESULTS|Conversely, the PPARgamma-Pro12Ala variant seems not to have a significant effect on T2D risk in our Tunisian cohort.
18657335|ab|7|18657335||RESULTS|RESULTS|However, the minor A-allele would convey protection against overweight in the Tunisian population.
18657335|ab|8|18657335||RESULTS|RESULTS|In fact, the over weighted subjects showed a significantly lower frequency of A-allele than lean controls (OR=0.49, 95%CI [0.25-0.97], p=0.02).
18657335|ab|9|18657335||CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|In conclusion, our findings support the hypothesis that ENPP1-121Q is involved in the genetic susceptibility of T2D in the Tunisian population, while the PPARgamma-12Ala allele may confer protection against overweight.

29953830|ab|4|29953830|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Forty-three studies met the review inclusion and exclusion criteria.
29953830|ab|5|29953830|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Physical exercise was the most common intervention approach.
29953830|ab|6|29953830|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Physical exercise interventions for frail older adults showed a moderate benefit, but no benefits were found for older adults without noticeable difficulty in ADLs.
29953830|ab|7|29953830|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|For older adults with difficulty in ADLs, there was a high benefit of using home-based intervention.
29953830|ab|8|29953830|CONCLUSION|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|The findings of this systematic review highlight the importance of addressing older adults' living environment in intervention to promote independence in ADLs.
22994439|ab|1|22994439||BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|The prevalence of heart failure (HF) in the population is increasing, concomitant with high incidence of rehospitalizations and mortality.
22994439|ab|2|22994439||OBJECTIVE|OBJECTIVE|The aim of this study was to characterize a prognostic risk score model for patients with chronic HF.
22994439|ab|3|22994439||METHODS|METHODS|A total of 500 patients followed at the HF clinic were evaluated by clinical, functional, laboratory, imaging, and therapeutic variables that were correlated to mortality during a follow-up period of 25 months.
22994439|ab|4|22994439||METHODS|METHODS|Risk stratification was carried out by applying a risk score model based on multivariate analysis.
22994439|ab|5|22994439||RESULTS|RESULTS|Predictors correlated with mortality during follow-up were systolic blood pressure <110 mm Hg, male sex, age older than 70 years, 6-minute walk distance <300 m, lack of beta-blocker therapy, hyperuricemia (>7.5 mg/dL), hyponatremia, and prolonged QTc interval (>450 ms).
22994439|ab|6|22994439||RESULTS|RESULTS|Based on these variables, a risk score model (score 0-55) was established and included low risk, score <21 (9% mortality during 2-year follow-up); moderate risk, 21 to 29 (22%); high risk, 30 to 35 (35%), and very high risk: >=36 points (62% 2-year mortality).
22994439|ab|7|22994439||RESULTS|RESULTS|The risk model had good discrimination ability (concordance index 0.75), which was better than the performance of the Seattle Heart Failure Model on our cohort (0.69).
22994439|ab|8|22994439||CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|Simple noninvasive characteristics examined during the initial admission to the HF clinic can serve as prognostic markers for mortality and may help in the process of therapeutic decision-making in patients with HF.
29957254|ab|1|29957254|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|Extracellular high-mobility group box 1 (HMGB1) has been identified as playing a critical role in the pathogenesis of tissue fibrosis.
29957254|ab|2|29957254|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|However, the underlying mechanism of its involvement in cardiac fibrosis is still not well-defined.

29957254|ab|5|29957254|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|Glycyrrhizic acid (GA), an inhibitor of HMGB1 derived from natural products, was simultaneously administered by intraperitoneal injection.
29957254|ab|6|29957254|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|Echocardiography, H&E and Sirius red staining were used to evaluate cardiac function and fibrosis.
29957254|ab|7|29957254|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|The myocardial expression of autophagy-associated proteins was examined using immunoblotting.
29957254|ab|8|29957254|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|Cardiac fibroblasts were treated with different concentrations of HMGB1 to examine the expression levels of alpha-SMA, collagen I and autophagy markers.
29957254|ab|9|29957254|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|Interactions of HMGB1/TLR2 and alpha-SMA/p62 were examined by immunoprecipitation and immunofluorescence.
29957254|ab|10|29957254|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|ISO-treated mice showed characteristic cardiac fibrosis, increased expression and co-localization of HMGB1 and TLR2, as well as impaired autophagic signals in myocardial tissues, which could be prevented by silencing TLR2.
29957254|ab|11|29957254|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Exogenous administration of HMGB1 blocked the autophagic flux in fibroblasts, which caused extensive accumulation of collagen I and alpha-SMA.
29957254|ab|12|29957254|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|In addition, cardiac fibrosis was alleviated by GA treatment through abrogating the interaction between HMGB1 and TLR2.
29957254|ab|13|29957254|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|Our study suggests that the interaction between TLR2 and HMGB1 contributes to the pathogenesis of cardiac fibrosis via suppressing fibroblast autophagy, and that inhibiting HMGB1 with GA provides therapeutic benefits for the treatment of fibroproliferative heart diseases.

26972210|ab|4|26972210||BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|Pharyngeal, respiratory, cardiac, and neck muscles may also be affected.

26972210|ab|6|26972210||BACKGROUND|RESULTS|Although the cutaneous manifestations in DM are variable, taken together, they represent a characteristic and crucial diagnostic criterion for DM.
26972210|ab|7|26972210||RESULTS|RESULTS|Approximately 5-20 % of individuals exhibit typical skin lesions without any clinically manifest muscle involvement (amyopathic DM).
26972210|ab|8|26972210||CONCLUSIONS|RESULTS|About 30 % of adult DM cases are associated with a malignancy.
26972210|ab|9|26972210||RESULTS|RESULTS|This fact, however, should not delay the treatment of severe myositis.

26972210|ab|19|26972210||CONCLUSIONS|RESULTS|UV protection is an important prophylactic measure.

22436841|ab|1|22436841||BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|Health benefits of physical activity may depend on a concomitant weight loss.
22436841|ab|2|22436841||OBJECTIVE|OBJECTIVE|In a randomized, controlled trial, we compared the effects of endurance training with or without weight loss to the effect of weight loss induced by an energy-reduced diet in 48 sedentary, moderately overweight men who completed a 12-week intervention program of training (T), energy-reduced diet (D), training and increased diet (T-iD), or control (C).
22436841|ab|3|22436841||METHODS|METHODS|An energy deficit of 600 kcal/day was induced by endurance training or diet in T and D and a similar training regimen plus an increased dietary intake of 600 kcal/day defined the T-iD group.
22436841|ab|4|22436841||METHODS|METHODS|Primary end point was insulin sensitivity as evaluated by HOMA-IR (mainly reflecting hepatic insulin sensitivity) and hyperinsulinemic, isoglycemic clamps (primarily reflecting peripheral insulin sensitivity).
22436841|ab|5|22436841||RESULTS|RESULTS|Body mass decreased in T and D by 5.9 +/- 0.7 and 5.3 +/- 0.7 kg, respectively, whereas T-iD and C remained weight stable.
22436841|ab|6|22436841||RESULTS|RESULTS|Total and abdominal fat mass were reduced in an additive manner in the T-iD, D, and T groups by 1.9 +/- 0.3/0.2 +/- 0.1, 4.4 +/- 0.7/0.5 +/- 0.1, and 7.7 +/- 0.8/0.9 +/- 0.1 kg, respectively.
22436841|ab|7|22436841||RESULTS|RESULTS|HOMA-IR was improved in T, D, and T-iD, whereas insulin-stimulated glucose clearance and suppression of plasma nonesterified fatty acids (NEFAs) were increased only in the two training groups.
22436841|ab|8|22436841||RESULTS|CONCLUSIONS|Thus, loss of fat mass (diet or training induced) improves hepatic insulin sensitivity, whereas peripheral insulin sensitivity in skeletal muscle and adipose tissue is increased by endurance training only.
22436841|ab|9|22436841||CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|This demonstrates that endurance training per se increases various metabolic health parameters and that endurance training should preferably always be included in any intervention regimen for improving metabolic health in moderately overweight men.
29865087|ab|1|29865087|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|Although adult and late-onset DM1 phenotypes DM1 present distinct lower limb weaknesses portraits, resulting physical limitations have never been described separately for each phenotype.
29865087|ab|2|29865087|OBJECTIVE|OBJECTIVE|OBJECTIVE|To characterize the lower limb weaknesses and physical limitations among the DM1 adult and late-onset phenotypes separately and to document the contribution of weaknesses on mobility to optimize the management of this population.
29865087|ab|3|29865087|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|The strength of four muscle groups among 198 participants was quantified.
29865087|ab|4|29865087|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|Participants were categorized according to the severity of their muscular involvement using the Muscular Impairment Rating Scale (MIRS).
29865087|ab|5|29865087|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|Physical limitations were assessed using the Timed up-and-go (TUG), Berg Balance Scale (BBS) and 10 meters comfortable walking speed (10MWT).
29865087|ab|6|29865087|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|Multiple linear regressions were performed to identify the contribution of each muscle group to the mobility tests scores.
29865087|ab|7|29865087|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Late-onset demonstrated less weakness and physical limitations (p < 0.001 - 0.002) than the adult phenotype, but 21.9-47.5% of participants with this phenotype showed mobility scores below reference values.
29865087|ab|8|29865087|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Physical limitations were observed in the first two MIRS grades (37.5-42.1% of the participants) for the TUG and 10MWT.
29865087|ab|9|29865087|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Ankle dorsiflexors and knee extensors were the two muscle groups that showed the strongest relationships with mobility scores.
29865087|ab|10|29865087|CONCLUSION|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|Although less impaired, the late-onset phenotype shows significant lower limb muscle weakness associated with physical limitations.
29865087|ab|11|29865087|CONCLUSION|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|The surprising presence of quantitative lower limb muscle weakness in the first two MIRS grades needs to be considered when using this scale.
29865087|ab|12|29865087|CONCLUSION|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|Both ankle dorsiflexors and knee extensors appear to be good indicators of physical limitations in DM1.
29957568|ab|1|29957568|OBJECTIVES|OBJECTIVE|BACKGROUND|The risk of drowning is reported to be 15-19 times greater in people with epilepsy compared to the general population.
29957568|ab|2|29957568|OBJECTIVES|OBJECTIVE|BACKGROUND|Despite this disproportionate burden, there is limited data about the circumstances surrounding drowning deaths in people with epilepsy.
29957568|ab|3|29957568|OBJECTIVES|OBJECTIVE|OBJECTIVE|This population-based case series characterizes drowning deaths in people with epilepsy.
29957568|ab|4|29957568|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|Postmortem data from coroner-ordered autopsies conducted in Ontario between 2014 and 2016 were screened for cases of drowning in people with a history of seizures.
29957568|ab|5|29957568|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|Demographic information, epilepsy characteristics, and circumstances surrounding death were extracted from post mortem reports.
29957568|ab|6|29957568|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|The incidence of drowning in people with epilepsy was calculated using government estimates of the Ontario population and the number of people with epilepsy.
29957568|ab|7|29957568|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Twenty-five people with epilepsy drowned during the three-year study period, giving an estimated incidence of 1.5 per 10,000 epilepsy person-years (95% CI: 0.98, 2.23).
29957568|ab|8|29957568|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Decedents were mostly young (mean age 36 years) and without physical or developmental disability.
29957568|ab|9|29957568|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Approximately one-third had psychiatric comorbidities.
29957568|ab|10|29957568|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Epilepsy severity ranged from well-controlled to drug refractory.
29957568|ab|11|29957568|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Only 3 people had alcohol or illicit drugs detected on toxicological analysis.
29957568|ab|12|29957568|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Forty-four percent of deaths were the result of an unwitnessed drowning in a bathtub.
29957568|ab|13|29957568|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|This population-based case series confirms people with epilepsy drown at a rate nearly ten times greater than the general population (1.5 per 10,000 epilepsy person-years compared to the estimated provincial average of 0.13 per 10,000).
29957568|ab|14|29957568|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|Drowning deaths in people with epilepsy most often occur in the bathtub.
29957568|ab|15|29957568|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|These deaths are only rarely associated with intoxication.
29957568|ab|16|29957568|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|People with epilepsy should receive counseling on the increased risk of drowning, including information regarding the significant risk associated with bathtub use, the potential protective roles of anti-epileptic drug (AED) adherence and supervision when in or around water, and the fact that all people with epilepsy remain at an increased risk of drowning regardless of their apparent seizure control.

19465701|ab|2|19465701||OBJECTIVE|OBJECTIVE|Based on recent data implicating vasoactive intestinal polypeptide (VIP) as the key intercellular synchronizing agent, we developed a multicellular SCN model to investigate the effects of cellular heterogeneity and intercellular connectivity on circadian behavior.
19465701|ab|3|19465701||METHODS|METHODS|A 2-dimensional grid was populated with 400 model cells that were heterogeneous with respect to their uncoupled rhythmic behavior (intrinsic and damped pacemakers with a range of oscillation periods) and VIP release characteristics (VIP producers and nonproducers).
19465701|ab|4|19465701||METHODS|METHODS|We constructed small-world network architectures in which local connections between VIP producing cells and their 4 nearest neighbors were augmented with random connections, resulting in long-range coupling across the grid.
19465701|ab|5|19465701||RESULTS|RESULTS|With only 10% of the total possible connections, the small-world network model was able to produce similar phase synchronization indices as a mean-field model with VIP producing cells connected to all other cells.
19465701|ab|6|19465701||RESULTS|RESULTS|Partial removal of random connections decreased the synchrony among neurons, the amplitude of VIP and cAMP response element binding protein oscillations, the mean period of intrinsic periods across the population, and the percentage of oscillating cells.
19465701|ab|7|19465701||CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|These results indicate that small-world connectivity provides the optimal compromise between the number of connections and control of circadian amplitude and synchrony.
19465701|ab|8|19465701||CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|This model predicts that small decreases in long-range VIP connections in the SCN could have dramatic effects on period and amplitude of daily rhythms, features commonly described with aging.

29876876|ab|6|29876876|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Caffeine has a small but evident effect on endurance performance when taken in moderate doses (3-6 mg/kg) as well as an overall improvement following caffeine compared to placebo in mean power output (3.03 +/- 3.07%; effect size = 0.23 +/- 0.15) and time-trial completion time (2.22 +/- 2.59%; effect size = 0.41 +/- 0.2).

29947341|ab|2|29947341|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|Although microglial activation acts as a key contributor in the neuroinflammatory response, the relationship between hemin and NLRP3 in microglia remains poorly understood.

29954662|ab|2|29954662|INTRODUCTION|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|The atmosphere and ocean have warmed, the amounts of snow and ice have diminished, the sea level has risen, and the concentrations of greenhouse gases have increased.
29954662|ab|3|29954662|INTRODUCTION|BACKGROUND|OBJECTIVE|This article will focus on climate change and projected effects on venomous marine and amphibious creatures with the potential impact on human health.
29954662|ab|4|29954662|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|Retrospective analysis of environmental, ecological, and medical literature with a focus on climate change, toxinology, and future modeling specific to venomous aquatic and amphibious creatures.

29954662|ab|7|29954662|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Habitat expansions by lionfish and sea snakes are projected to occur.

29954662|ab|11|29954662|CONCLUSION|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|Review of the literature investigating the effect and forecasts of climate change on venomous marine and amphibious creatures has demonstrated that temperature extremes and changes to climatic norms will likely have a dramatic effect on these toxicological organisms.
29954662|ab|12|29954662|CONCLUSION|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|The effects of climate change on these species through temperature alteration and rising coastal waters will influence each species differently and in turn potentially affect commercial industries, travel, tourism, and human health.

29935728|ab|8|29935728|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|RESULTS|Airborne-particle abrasion resulted in a significant increase in surface roughness compared with the other groups.
29935728|ab|9|29935728|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|RESULTS|After nonthermal plasma treatment, the contact angle of the zirconia surface decreased within 48 hours.
29935728|ab|10|29935728|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|Nonthermal plasma application for surface treatment of zirconia showed no significant difference in bond strength when compared with airborne-particle abrasion.

29903694|ab|7|29903694|RESULTS|RESULTS|METHODS|Posts from Facebook (143/227, 63.0%) and Instagram (84/227, 37.0%) were included.
29903694|ab|8|29903694|RESULTS|RESULTS|METHODS|Photos (64%) and videos (34%) were used to enhance most posts.
29903694|ab|9|29903694|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Different strategies were most effective for Facebook and Instagram.
29903694|ab|10|29903694|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Strategies associated with higher Facebook interactions included links to purchasable items (beta=0.81, 95% CI 0.50 to 1.13, P<.001) featuring body image messages compared with food content (beta=1.96, 95% CI 1.29 to 2.64, P<.001), and where the content induced positive emotions (beta=0.31, 95% CI 0.04 to 0.57, P=.02).
29903694|ab|11|29903694|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Facebook interactions were negatively associated with using pop culture (beta=-0.67, 95% CI -0.99 to -0.34, P<.001), storytelling (beta=-0.86, 95% CI -1.29 to -0.43, P<.001) or visually appealing graphics (beta=-0.53, 95% CI -0.78 to -0.28, P<.001) in their posts compared with other strategies.
29903694|ab|12|29903694|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Posting relatable content was negatively associated with interactions on Facebook (beta=-0.29, 95% CI -0.53 to -0.06, P=.01), but positively associated on Instagram (beta=0.50, 95% CI 0.05 to 0.95, P=.03).
29903694|ab|13|29903694|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Instagram interactions were negatively associated with weight loss (beta=-1.45, 95% CI -2.69 to -0.21, P=.02) and other content (beta=-0.81, 95% CI -1.57 to -.06, P=.04) compared with food content.
29903694|ab|14|29903694|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|Health promotion professionals and organizations can improve engagement using positive messaging and tailoring posts appropriate for different social media channels.

29926483|ab|2|29926483|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|However, the evidence underpinning this topic is unclear and no systematic review has yet been conducted.

29926483|ab|6|29926483|DATA SOURCES|METHODS|METHODS|Prospective, longitudinal observational studies with follow-up of at least 12 months and presenting data on the primary outcome, change in clinical attachment level, in adults (age >/=18 years).
29926483|ab|7|29926483|DATA SOURCES|METHODS|METHODS|Secondary outcomes, tooth loss and bone level change, were only assessed in studies reporting the primary outcome.

29926483|ab|13|29926483|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|The studies represented populations from both developing and developed economies.
29926483|ab|14|29926483|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Mean annual attachment loss was 0.1 mm per year (95% CI 0.068, 0.132; I(2 ) = 99%) and mean annual tooth loss was 0.2 teeth per year (95% CI 0.10, 0.33; I(2 ) = 94%).
29926483|ab|15|29926483|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Observational analysis of highest and lowest mean attachment change quintiles suggested substantial differences between groups with minimal annual change in the lowest quintile and an average deterioration of 0.45 mm mean attachment loss per year in the highest group.

29926483|ab|19|29926483|LIMITATIONS|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|There were a limited number of studies (N = 16), high variability of design in key study components (sampling frames, included ages, data analyses), and high statistical heterogeneity that could not be explained.
29926483|ab|20|29926483|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|Within the limitations of the research, the data show that mean annual attachment level change varies considerably both within and between populations.
29926483|ab|21|29926483|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|Overall, the evidence does not support or refute the differentiation between forms of periodontal diseases based upon progression of attachment level change.

21911402|ab|5|21911402||RESULTS|RESULTS|Fluorescence microscopy and stretching experiments reveal that the metastable states are the result of intramolecular self-entanglements induced by the electric field.
21911402|ab|6|21911402||CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|These results have broad importance in DNA separations and single molecule genomics, polymer rheology, and DNA-based nanofabrication.

29940078|ab|1|29940078|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|Corneal endothelial transplantation has become the gold standard for the treatment of corneal endothelial dysfunctions, replacing full thickness transplantation, known as penetrating keratoplasty.
29940078|ab|2|29940078|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|Corneal endothelial transplantation has been described using two different techniques: Descemet's membrane endothelial keratoplasty (DMEK) and Descemet's stripping automated endothelial keratoplasty (DSAEK).
29940078|ab|3|29940078|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|Both are still performed worldwide.
29940078|ab|4|29940078|OBJECTIVES|OBJECTIVE|OBJECTIVE|To compare the effectiveness and safety of Descemet's membrane endothelial keratoplasty (DMEK) versus Descemet's stripping automated endothelial keratoplasty (DSAEK) for the treatment of corneal endothelial failure in people with Fuch's endothelial dystropy (FED) and pseudophakic bullous keratopathy (PBK).
29940078|ab|6|29940078|SEARCH METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|The date of the search was 11 August 2017.
29940078|ab|7|29940078|SELECTION CRITERIA|METHODS|METHODS|We included randomised controlled trials (RCTs) and non-randomised paired, contralateral-eye studies in any setting where DMEK was compared with DSAEK to treat people with corneal endothelial failure.
29940078|ab|8|29940078|SELECTION CRITERIA|METHODS|METHODS|Two review authors independently screened the search results, assessed trial quality and extracted data using the standard methodological procedures expected by Cochrane.
29940078|ab|9|29940078|SELECTION CRITERIA|METHODS|METHODS|Our primary outcome was best corrected visual acuity (BCVA) measured in logarithm of the Minimum Angle of Resolution (logMAR).
29940078|ab|10|29940078|SELECTION CRITERIA|METHODS|METHODS|Secondary outcomes were endothelial cell count, graft rejection, primary graft failure and graft dislocation.
29940078|ab|11|29940078|SELECTION CRITERIA|METHODS|METHODS|We graded the risk of bias of non-randomised studies (NRSs) using ROBINS-I.
29940078|ab|12|29940078|MAIN RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|We did not identify any RCTs but found four non-randomised studies (NRSs) including 72 participants (144 eyes), who had received DSAEK in the first eye followed by DMEK in the fellow eye.
29940078|ab|13|29940078|MAIN RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|All the studies included adult participants where there was evidence of FED and endothelial failure requiring a corneal transplant for the treatment of visual impairment.
29940078|ab|14|29940078|MAIN RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|We did not find any studies that included PBK.
29940078|ab|15|29940078|MAIN RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|The trials were published between 2011 and 2015, and we assessed them as high risk of bias due to potential unknown confounding factors since DSAEK preceded DMEK in all participants.
29940078|ab|16|29940078|MAIN RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Two studies reported results at 12 months, one at 6 months, and one between 6 and 24 months.
29940078|ab|17|29940078|MAIN RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|At one year, using DMEK in cases of endothelial failure may result in better BCVA compared with DSAEK (mean difference (MD) -0.14, 95% confidence interval (CI) -0.18 to -0.10 logMAR, 4 studies, 140 eyes, low-certainty evidence).
29940078|ab|18|29940078|MAIN RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|None of the participants had severe visual loss (BCVA of 1.0 logMAR or more; very low-certainty evidence).
29940078|ab|19|29940078|MAIN RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Regarding endothelial cell count data (4 studies, 134 eyes) it is hard to draw any conclusions since two studies suggested no difference and the other two reported that DMEK provides a higher cell density at one year (very low-certainty evidence).
29940078|ab|20|29940078|MAIN RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|No primary graft failure and only one graft rejection were recorded over four studies (144 eyes) (very low-certainty evidence).
29940078|ab|21|29940078|MAIN RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|The most common complications reported were graft dislocations, which were recorded in one or two out of 100 participants with DSAEK but were more common using DMEK, although this difference could not be precisely estimated (risk ratio (RR) 5.40, 95% CI 1.51 to 19.3; 4 studies, 144 eyes, very low-certainty evidence).
29940078|ab|22|29940078|AUTHORS' CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|This review included studies conducted on people with corneal endothelium failure due to FED for whom both DMEK and DSAEK can be considered, and found low-certainty evidence that DMEK provides some advantage in terms of final BCVA, at the cost of more graft dislocations needing 're-bubbling' (very low-certainty of evidence).

29953478|ab|2|29953478|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|Thirty-seven patients (mean age: 45+/-13 y) with newly diagnosed gliomas and dynamic 18F-FET PET before any histopathologic investigation or treatment were retrospectively included.

29953478|ab|4|29953478|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|A tumor mask was semi-automatically generated from Z-score maps.
29953478|ab|5|29953478|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|Each brain tumor voxel was clustered in one of the 3 following centroids using dynamic time warping and k-means clustering (centroid #1: slowly increasing slope; centroid #2: rapidly increasing followed by slowly decreasing slope; and centroid #3: rapidly increasing followed by rapidly decreasing slope).
29953478|ab|6|29953478|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|The percentage of each dynamic 18F-FET TAC within tumors and other conventional 18F-FET PET parameters (maximum and mean tumor-to-brain ratios [TBRmax and TBRmean], time-to-peak [TTP] and slope) was compared between wild-type and IDH1 mutant tumors.
29953478|ab|7|29953478|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|Their prognostic value was assessed in terms of progression free-survival (PFS) and overall survival (OS) by Kaplan-Meier estimates.
29953478|ab|8|29953478|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Twenty patients were IDH1 wild-type and 17 IDH1 mutant.
29953478|ab|9|29953478|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Higher percentage of centroid #1 and centroid #3 within tumors were positively (P = 0.016) and negatively (P = 0.01) correlated with IDH1 mutated status.
29953478|ab|10|29953478|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Also, TBRmax, TBRmean, TTP, and slope discriminated significantly between tumors with and without IDH1 mutation (P range 0.01 to 0.04).
29953478|ab|11|29953478|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Progression occurred in 22 patients (59%) at a median of 13.1 months (7.6-37.6 months) and 13 patients (35%) died from tumor progression.
29953478|ab|12|29953478|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Patients with a percentage of centroid #1 > 90% had a longer survival compared with those with a percentage of centroid #1 < 90% (P = 0.003 for PFS and P = 0.028 for OS).
29953478|ab|13|29953478|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|This remained significant after stratification on IDH1 mutation status (P = 0.029 for PFS and P = 0.034 for OS).
29953478|ab|14|29953478|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Compared to other conventional 18F-FET PET parameters, TTP and slope were associated with PFS and OS (P range 0.009 to 0.04).
29953478|ab|15|29953478|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|Based on dynamic 18F-FET PET acquisition, we developed a full automatic clustering approach of TAC which appears to be a valuable noninvasive diagnostic and prognostic marker in patients with gliomas.

29948973|ab|1|29948973|PURPOSE|OBJECTIVE|OBJECTIVE|To assess the impact of bloodstream infection (BSI) in patients with head and neck cancer (HNC) in the cetuximab era.
29948973|ab|2|29948973|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|We prospectively analysed the epidemiology, microbiology and outcomes of 51 BSI episodes occurring in 48 patients with HNC (2006-2017).
29948973|ab|3|29948973|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|We performed a retrospective matched-cohort study (1:2) to determine the risk factors for BSI.
29948973|ab|4|29948973|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|Finally, we compared patients who died with those who survived to identify risk factors for mortality.
29948973|ab|5|29948973|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|The most frequent HNC localization was the oropharynx (43%), and pneumonia was the most frequent source (25%).
29948973|ab|6|29948973|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Gram-positive BSI occurred in 55% cases, mainly due to Streptococcus pneumoniae (21%), and among Gram-negatives, Escherichia coli, Pseudomonas aeruginosa, and Klebsiella pneumoniae were the most frequent.
29948973|ab|7|29948973|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Hypoalbuminemia (OR 8.4; 95% CI, 3.5-19.9), previous chemotherapy (OR, 3.2; 95% CI, 1.3-7.4) and cetuximab therapy (OR, 2.8; 95% CI, 1.6-6.7) were significant risk factors for BSI.
29948973|ab|8|29948973|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Patients with BSI had a higher overall case-fatality rate than patients without BSI (OR, 4.4; 95% CI, 1.7-11.8).
29948973|ab|9|29948973|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Hypoalbuminemia was an independent risk factor for the early (7 day) and overall (30 day) case-fatalities, with ORs of 0.8 (95% CI, 0.6-0.9) and 0.8 (95% CI, 0.7-0.97), respectively.
29948973|ab|10|29948973|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|The presence of comorbidities (OR, 7; 95% CI, 1.4-34) was also an independent risk factor for overall case-fatality.
29948973|ab|11|29948973|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|BSI causes high mortality in patients with HNC and is most often secondary to pneumonia.
29948973|ab|12|29948973|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|It occurs mainly among patients with hypoalbuminemia who receive treatment with cetuximab or chemotherapy.
29948973|ab|13|29948973|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|The development of BSI in patients with HNC impairs their outcome, especially in the presence of hypoalbuminemia and comorbidities.
29945293|ab|1|29945293|AIMS AND OBJECTIVES|OBJECTIVE|OBJECTIVE|To compare and evaluate the reliability, validity, feasibility, clinical utility, and nurses' preference of the Premature Infant Pain Profile-Revised, the Neonatal Pain, Agitation, and Sedation Scale, and the Neonatal Infant Acute Pain Assessment Scale used for procedural pain in ventilated neonates.
29945293|ab|2|29945293|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|Procedural pain is a common phenomenon but is undermanaged and underassessed in hospitalised neonates.
29945293|ab|3|29945293|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|Information for clinician selecting pain measurements to improve neonatal care and outcomes is still limited.
29945293|ab|4|29945293|DESIGN|METHODS|METHODS|A prospective observational study was used.
29945293|ab|5|29945293|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|A total of 1,080 pain assessments were made at 90 neonates by two nurses independently, using three scales viewing three phases of videotaped painful (arterial blood sampling) and nonpainful procedures (diaper change).
29945293|ab|6|29945293|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|Internal consistency, inter-rater reliability, discriminant validity, concurrent validity and convergent validity of scales were analysed.
29945293|ab|7|29945293|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|Feasibility, clinical utility and nurses' preference of scales were also investigated.
29945293|ab|8|29945293|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|All three scales showed excellent inter-rater coefficients (from 0.991-0.992) and good internal consistency (0.733 for the Premature Infant Pain Profile-Revised, 0.837 for the Neonatal Pain, Agitation, and Sedation Scale and 0.836 for the Neonatal Infant Acute Pain Assessment Scale, respectively).
29945293|ab|9|29945293|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Scores of painful and nonpainful procedures on the three scales changed significantly across the phases.
29945293|ab|10|29945293|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|There was a strong correlation between the three scales with adequate limits of agreement.
29945293|ab|11|29945293|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|The mean scores of the Neonatal Pain, Agitation, and Sedation Scale for feasibility and utility were significantly higher than those of the Neonatal Infant Acute Pain Assessment Scale, but not significantly higher than those of the Premature Infant Pain Profile-Revised.
29945293|ab|12|29945293|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|The Neonatal Pain, Agitation, and Sedation Scale was mostly preferred by 55.9% of the nurses, followed by the Neonatal Infant Acute Pain Assessment Scale (23.5%) and the Premature Infant Pain Profile-Revised (20.6%).
29945293|ab|13|29945293|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|The three scales are all reliable and valid, but the Neonatal Pain, Agitation, and Sedation Scale and the Neonatal Infant Acute Pain Assessment Scale perform better in reliability.
29945293|ab|14|29945293|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|The Neonatal Pain, Agitation, and Sedation Scale appears to be a better choice for frontier nurses to assess procedural pain in ventilated neonates based on its good feasibility, utility and nurses' preference.
29945293|ab|15|29945293|RELEVANCE TO CLINICAL PRACTICE|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|Choosing a valid, reliable, feasible and practical measurement is the key step for better management of procedural pain for ventilated newborns.
29945293|ab|16|29945293|RELEVANCE TO CLINICAL PRACTICE|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|Using the right and suitable tool is helpful to accurately identify pain, ultimately improve the neonatal care and outcomes.
29953657|ab|1|29953657|AIMS|OBJECTIVE|OBJECTIVE|The aim of this systematic review and meta-analysis was to determine the impact of lower urinary tract symptoms (LUTS) on work productivity in female workers.
29953657|ab|2|29953657|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|A comprehensive literature search was conducted using eight electronic databases (MEDLINE, PEDro, CINAHL, Cochrane library, EMBASE, PubMed, Scopus, and PsycINFO) to identify articles published before July 2017 that studied the work productivity in female workers with LUTS.
29953657|ab|3|29953657|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|Two reviewers independently assessed the quality of studies using the Joanna Briggs Institute.
29953657|ab|4|29953657|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|Meta-analyses were performed on studies having measured work productivity between females with and without LUTS, and odds ratios (ORs) or the mean differences were used.
29953657|ab|5|29953657|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Fourteen articles (n = 48 223 females) were included in the review, and meta-analyses were performed with six of those articles.
29953657|ab|6|29953657|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Lower urinary tract symptoms were significantly associated with work productivity loss (OR = 1.11, 95%CI = 1.06-1.15), presenteeism (OR = 1.10, 95%CI = 1.05-1.14), and activity impairment (OR = 1.11, 95%CI = 1.09-1.14).
29953657|ab|7|29953657|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|However, there was no significant difference in the probability of absenteeism between females with and without LUTS (OR = 1.03, 95%CI = 0.94-1.13).
29953657|ab|8|29953657|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|Evidence suggests that female workers with LUTS had significantly greater work productivity impairment compared to those without LUTS.
29954018|ab|1|29954018|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|Stress increases the risk of developing and maintaining alcohol addiction.
29954018|ab|2|29954018|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|Mechanism for reacting to, and coping with, stress in persons with alcohol addiction are an important factor enabling them to maintain abstinence in everyday life.
29954018|ab|3|29954018|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|Also of Relevance for abstinence, and in particular craving for alcohol, is the severity of the dependence.
29954018|ab|4|29954018|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|Numerous studies have focused on the duration of abstinence, but not on the severity of the disease.
29954018|ab|5|29954018|OBJECTIVE|OBJECTIVE|OBJECTIVE|This study investigates if, in addition to abstinence duration, also the severity of the alcohol addiction influences stress responsiveness and ability to cope with stress.
29954018|ab|6|29954018|OBJECTIVE|OBJECTIVE|OBJECTIVE|Another objective is to ascertain in which patients such an influence can be found.
29954018|ab|7|29954018|OBJECTIVE|OBJECTIVE|OBJECTIVE|The results can shed light on the complex bidirectional relationship between alcoholism and stress, but are also potentially useful in treating patients with this disease.
29954018|ab|8|29954018|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|In a cross-sectional design, 64 alcohol-dependent patients and 30 healthy controls were examined.
29954018|ab|9|29954018|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|The alcoholics sample was divided in two groups according to a duration of abstinence of seven days and, 70 days.
29954018|ab|10|29954018|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|Each group was further divided in a subgroup of individuals with mild to moderate alcohol addiction and in a subgroup of patients with severe alcohol addiction (A7-severe and A70-severe).
29954018|ab|11|29954018|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|Using the Trierer Social Stress Test (TSST), all participants were subjected to acute stress.
29954018|ab|12|29954018|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|Parameters measured were salivary cortisol, skin conductance -response, heart rate, addiction-related variables (addiction severity, duration of alcohol abuse, drinking quantity, craving, liver enzymes, family history of alcoholism, number of therapies, smoking), psychopathological variables (anxiety, depression, live events, personality disorders), acute and long-term stress coping, and level of strain on everyday life.
29954018|ab|13|29954018|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|In patients with severe addiction, the reaction to stress is weaker and slightly retarded, but also of a longer duration than that patients with mild and moderate addiction and of healthy controls.
29954018|ab|14|29954018|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|This is independent of the length of abstinence (7 days and 70 days).
29954018|ab|15|29954018|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|In severely ill patients, strategies for coping with acute stress differed from those of the other groups in that they consisted in stronger flight and avoidance responses, a stronger need for social support, and a more intense mental preoccupation.
29954018|ab|16|29954018|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Increased levels of social tension, lack of social recognition, and isolation indicated chronic stress.
29954018|ab|17|29954018|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Patients with severe alcohol addiction also showed a more pronounced familial predisposition, stronger craving, increased anxiety, a longer history of alcohol abuse, and a higher frequency of incisive life events than patients with mild to moderate alcohol addiction.
29954018|ab|18|29954018|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|The results indicate that a more differentiated evaluation of stress responsiveness and stress coping in persons with an alcohol addiction not only length of abstinence, but also severity of disease have to be taken into account.
29954018|ab|19|29954018|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|Further research is necessary to adjust treatment accordingly.
20007704|ab|1|20007704||BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|In gamma-aminobutyric acid type A (GABA(A)) receptors, the structural elements that couple ligand binding to channel opening remain poorly defined.
20007704|ab|2|20007704||OBJECTIVE|OBJECTIVE|Here, site-directed mutagenesis was used to determine if Loop 9 on the non-GABA binding site interface of the beta2-subunit may be involved in GABA(A) receptor activation.
20007704|ab|3|20007704||METHODS|METHODS|Specifically, residues Gly(170)-Gln(185) of the beta2-subunit were mutated to alanine, co-expressed with wild-type alpha1- and gamma2S-subunits in human embryonic kidney (HEK) 293 cells and assayed for their activation by GABA, the intravenous anesthetic propofol and the endogenous neurosteroid pregnanolone using whole cell macroscopic recordings.
20007704|ab|4|20007704||RESULTS|RESULTS|Three mutants, G170A, V175A, and G177A, produced 2.5-, 6.7-, and 5.6-fold increases in GABA EC(50) whereas one mutant, Q185A, produced a 5.2-fold decrease in GABA EC(50).
20007704|ab|5|20007704||RESULTS|RESULTS|None of the mutations affected the ability of propofol or pregnanolone to potentiate a submaximal GABA response, but the Q185A mutant exhibited 8.3- and 3.5-fold increases in the percent direct activation by propofol and pregnanolone, respectively.
20007704|ab|6|20007704||RESULTS|RESULTS|Mutant Q185A receptors also had an increased leak current that was sensitive to picrotoxin, indicating an increased gating efficiency.
20007704|ab|7|20007704||RESULTS|RESULTS|Further Q185E, Q185L, and Q185W substitutions revealed a strong correlation between the hydropathy of the amino acid at this position and the GABA EC(50).
20007704|ab|8|20007704||CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|Taken together, these results indicate that beta2 Loop 9 is involved in receptor activation by GABA, propofol, and pregnanolone and that beta2(Q185) participates in hydrophilic interactions that are important for stabilizing the closed state of the GABA(A) receptor.
29901572|ab|1|29901572|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|Lowering the likelihood of hospitalization in older adults is a major public health goal for modern health care systems.
29901572|ab|2|29901572|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|Emerging data suggest that financial literacy is an important determinant of health outcomes in old age, but the relationship with hospitalization has not been explored.
29901572|ab|3|29901572|OBJECTIVE|OBJECTIVE|OBJECTIVE|To test the hypothesis that better financial literacy is related to lower risk of hospitalization in older persons.
29901572|ab|4|29901572|DESIGN|METHODS|METHODS|Prospective cohort study.
29901572|ab|5|29901572|PARTICIPANTS|METHODS|METHODS|Data came from community-dwelling older adults (n=388) without dementia enrolled in the Rush Memory and Aging Project.
29901572|ab|6|29901572|MAIN MEASURES|METHODS|METHODS|Participants underwent detailed assessment of financial literacy and cognition.
29901572|ab|7|29901572|MAIN MEASURES|METHODS|METHODS|Data on hospitalizations were obtained from linked Medicare claims records (MedPAR file).
29901572|ab|8|29901572|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Over an average of 1.8 years, 117 participants (30%) were hospitalized, and a third of those hospitalized experienced multiple hospitalizations.
29901572|ab|9|29901572|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|In a modified Poisson regression model adjusted for age, sex, education, and cognition, better financial literacy was associated with lower risk of hospitalization.
29901572|ab|10|29901572|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|In a model further adjusted for income, physical activity, body mass index, smoking, social network size, chronic conditions, basic and instrumental activities of daily living disability, and depressive symptoms, the association was unchanged.
29901572|ab|11|29901572|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Secondary analyses showed the association was primarily driven by conceptual knowledge rather than numeracy.
29901572|ab|12|29901572|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|Higher financial literacy is related to a lower risk of hospitalization in older persons without dementia, after adjusting for cognitive, health, functional, and socioeconomic factors.
29901572|ab|13|29901572|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|The ability to understand and utilize financial concepts may represent a potentially modifiable risk factor for hospitalization in later life.

19587052|ab|3|19587052||BACKGROUND|RESULTS|Based on characterization by functional ontology and known human-HIV protein interactions, we observed the enrichment for protein abundance increases pertaining to protein synthesis and nucleasomal reorganization amid an otherwise placid cellular proteome at the first sign of HIV replication.

16844342|ab|2|16844342||BACKGROUND|OBJECTIVE|In this study, we show that constitutively active protein phosphatase 2A (PP2A), which is a serine/threonine phosphatase, is essential for T leukemia cell survival.

16844342|ab|4|16844342||RESULTS|RESULTS|In addition, caspase-8 or caspase-9 inhibition with z-IETD-fmk or z-LEHD-fmk, respectively, largely prevented OA-induced apoptosis.

16844342|ab|7|16844342||RESULTS|RESULTS|In addition, caspase-9 and caspase-3 inhibition largely prevented procaspase-3 and procaspase-8 cleavage, respectively, while caspase-8 inhibition partially interfered with procaspase-9 cleavage in OA-treated T leukemia cells.
16844342|ab|8|16844342||RESULTS|RESULTS|Thus, PP2A inhibition triggered the intrinsic pathway of apoptosis, which was enhanced by a mitochondrial feedback amplification loop.

16844342|ab|11|16844342||RESULTS|RESULTS|Moreover, OA treatment caused p38 MAPK to be phosphorylated in a dose- and time-dependent fashion, indicating that PP2A prevented p38 MAPK activation.
16844342|ab|12|16844342||RESULTS|RESULTS|Although p38 MAPK activation usually promotes apoptosis, pharmacologic inhibition of p38 MAPK exacerbated OA-induced DNA fragmentation and loss of delta psi(m) in T leukemia cells, suggesting that, in this instance, the p38 MAPK signaling pathway promoted cell survival.
16844342|ab|13|16844342||CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|Collectively, these findings indicate that PP2A and p38 MAPK have coordinate effects on signaling pathways that regulate the survival of T leukemia cells.

29923841|ab|1|29923841|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|Cyanoacrylates, also known as tissue adhesives or skin glues, are commonly used as sealants for lacerations and incisions and have found utility in excisional and cosmetic surgeries in both outpatient and operating room settings.

29923841|ab|5|29923841|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Tissue adhesives polymerize to a water resistant, pliable film after application to approximated wound edges and have antibacterial properties.
29923841|ab|6|29923841|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Adhesives slowly slough off as the wound heals, typically after 5 days.
29923841|ab|7|29923841|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Compared with 5-0 nonabsorbable suture, adhesives provide similar tensile strength and similar patient and surgeon satisfaction.
29923841|ab|8|29923841|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Although slightly more expensive than sutures, tissue adhesives obviate the need for wound dressings and suture removal.
29923841|ab|9|29923841|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|They do not perform as well as sutures for wounds under higher tension or in the setting of moisture and inadequate hemostasis.
29923841|ab|10|29923841|CONCLUSION|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|Cyanoacrylates serve as a safe and effective suture alternative in appropriate dermatologic surgeries and procedures.

29938789|ab|1|29938789|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|Asthma is a chronic respiratory condition that affects over 300 million adults and children worldwide.
29938789|ab|2|29938789|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|It is characterised by wheeze, cough, chest tightness, and shortness of breath.
29938789|ab|3|29938789|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|Symptoms typically are intermittent and may worsen over a short time, leading to an exacerbation.
29938789|ab|4|29938789|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|Asthma exacerbations can be serious, leading to hospitalisation or even death in rare cases.
29938789|ab|5|29938789|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|Exacerbations may be treated by increasing an individual's usual medication and providing additional medication, such as oral steroids.
29938789|ab|6|29938789|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|Although antibiotics are sometimes included in the treatment regimen, bacterial infections are thought to be responsible for only a minority of exacerbations, and current guidance states that antibiotics should be reserved for cases in which clear signs, symptoms, or laboratory test results are suggestive of bacterial infection.
29938789|ab|7|29938789|OBJECTIVES|OBJECTIVE|OBJECTIVE|To determine the efficacy and safety of antibiotics in the treatment of asthma exacerbations.
29938789|ab|8|29938789|SEARCH METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|We searched the Cochrane Airways Trials Register, which contains records compiled from multiple electronic and handsearched resources.
29938789|ab|9|29938789|SEARCH METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|We also searched trial registries and reference lists of primary studies.
29938789|ab|10|29938789|SEARCH METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|We conducted the most recent search in October 2017.
29938789|ab|11|29938789|SELECTION CRITERIA|METHODS|METHODS|We included studies comparing antibiotic therapy for asthma exacerbations in adults or children versus placebo or usual care not involving an antibiotic.
29938789|ab|12|29938789|SELECTION CRITERIA|METHODS|METHODS|We allowed studies including any type of antibiotic, any dose, and any duration, providing the aim was to treat the exacerbation.
29938789|ab|13|29938789|SELECTION CRITERIA|METHODS|METHODS|We included parallel studies of any duration conducted in any setting and planned to include cluster trials.
29938789|ab|14|29938789|SELECTION CRITERIA|METHODS|METHODS|We excluded cross-over trials.
29938789|ab|15|29938789|SELECTION CRITERIA|METHODS|METHODS|We included studies reported as full-text articles, those published as abstracts only, and unpublished data.
29938789|ab|16|29938789|SELECTION CRITERIA|METHODS|METHODS|At least two review authors screened the search results for eligible studies.
29938789|ab|17|29938789|SELECTION CRITERIA|METHODS|METHODS|We extracted outcome data, assessed risk of bias in duplicate, and resolved discrepancies by involving another review author.
29938789|ab|18|29938789|SELECTION CRITERIA|METHODS|METHODS|We analysed dichotomous data as odds ratios (ORs) or risk differences (RDs), and continuous data as mean differences (MDs), all with a fixed-effect model.
29938789|ab|19|29938789|SELECTION CRITERIA|METHODS|METHODS|We described skewed data narratively.
29938789|ab|20|29938789|SELECTION CRITERIA|METHODS|METHODS|We graded the results and presented evidence in 'Summary of findings' tables for each comparison.
29938789|ab|21|29938789|SELECTION CRITERIA|METHODS|METHODS|Primary outcomes were intensive care unit/high dependence unit (ICU/HDU) admission, duration of symptoms/exacerbations, and all adverse events.
29938789|ab|22|29938789|SELECTION CRITERIA|METHODS|METHODS|Seconday outcomes were mortality, length of hospital admission, relapse after index presentation, and peak expiratory flow rate (PEFR).
29938789|ab|23|29938789|MAIN RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Six studies met our inclusion criteria and included a total of 681 adults and children with exacerbations of asthma.
29938789|ab|24|29938789|MAIN RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Mean age in the three studies in adults ranged from 36.2 to 41.2 years.
29938789|ab|25|29938789|MAIN RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|The three studies in children applied varied inclusion criteria, ranging from one to 18 years of age.
29938789|ab|26|29938789|MAIN RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Five studies explicitly excluded participants with obvious signs and symptoms of bacterial infection (i.e. those clearly meeting current guidance to receive antibiotics).
29938789|ab|27|29938789|MAIN RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Four studies investigated macrolide antibiotics, and two studies investigated penicillin (amoxicillin and ampicillin) antibiotics; both studies using penicillin were conducted over 35 years ago.
29938789|ab|28|29938789|MAIN RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Five studies compared antibiotics versus placebo, and one was open-label.
29938789|ab|29|29938789|MAIN RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Study follow-up ranged from one to twelve weeks.
29938789|ab|30|29938789|MAIN RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Trials were of varied methodological quality, and we were able to perform only limited meta-analysis.
29938789|ab|31|29938789|MAIN RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|None of the included trials reported ICU/HDU admission, although one participant in the placebo group of a study including children with status asthmaticus experienced a respiratory arrest and was ventilated.
29938789|ab|32|29938789|MAIN RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Four studies reported asthma symptoms, but we were able to combine results for only two macrolide studies of 416 participants; the MD in diary card symptom score was -0.34 (95% confidence interval (CI) -0.60 to -0.08), with lower scores (on a 7 point scale) denoting improved symptoms.
29938789|ab|33|29938789|MAIN RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Two macrolide studies reported symptom-free days.
29938789|ab|34|29938789|MAIN RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|One study of 255 adults authors reported the percentage of symptom-free days at 10 days as 16% in the antibiotic group and 8% in the placebo group.
29938789|ab|35|29938789|MAIN RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|In a further study of 40 children study authors reported significantly more symptom-free days at all time points in the antibiotic group compared with the usual care group.
29938789|ab|36|29938789|MAIN RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|The same study reported the duration in days of the index asthma exacerbation, again favouring the antibiotic group.
29938789|ab|37|29938789|MAIN RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|One study of a penicillin including 69 participants reported asthma symptoms at hospital discharge; the between-group difference for both studies was reported as non-significant.We combined data for serious adverse events from three studies involving 502 participants, but events were rare; the three trials reported only 10 events: five in the antibiotic group and five in the placebo group.
29938789|ab|38|29938789|MAIN RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|We combined data for all adverse events (AEs) from three studies, but the effect estimate is imprecise (OR 0.99, 95% CI 0.69 to 1.43).
29938789|ab|39|29938789|MAIN RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|No deaths were reported in any of the included studies.Two studies investigating penicillins reported admission duration; neither study reported a between-group difference.
29938789|ab|40|29938789|MAIN RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|In one study (263 participants) of macrolides, two participants in each arm were reported as experiencing a relapse, defined as a further exacerbation, by the six-week time points.
29938789|ab|41|29938789|MAIN RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|We combined PEFR endpoint results at 10 days for two macrolide studies; the result favoured antibiotics over placebo (MD 23.42 L/min, 95% CI 5.23 to 41.60).
29938789|ab|42|29938789|MAIN RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|One study in children reported the maximum peak flow recorded during the follow-up period, favouring the clarithromycin group, but the confidence interval includes no difference (MD 38.80, 95% CI -11.19 to 88.79).
29938789|ab|43|29938789|MAIN RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Grading of outcomes ranged from moderate to very low quality, with quality of outcomes downgraded for suspicion of publication bias, indirectness, imprecision, and poor methodological quality of studies.
29938789|ab|44|29938789|AUTHORS' CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|We found limited evidence that antibiotics given at the time of an asthma exacerbation may improve symptoms and PEFR at follow-up compared with standard care or placebo.
29938789|ab|45|29938789|AUTHORS' CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|However, findings were inconsistent across the six heterogeneous studies included, two of the studies were conducted over 30 years ago and most of the participants included in this review were recruited from emergency departments, limiting the applicability of findings to this population.
29938789|ab|46|29938789|AUTHORS' CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|Therefore we have limited confidence in the results.
29938789|ab|47|29938789|AUTHORS' CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|We found insufficient evidence about several patient-important outcomes (e.g. hospital admission) to form conclusions.
29938789|ab|48|29938789|AUTHORS' CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|We were unable to rule out a difference between groups in terms of all adverse events, but serious adverse events were rare.

29936188|ab|1|29936188|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|Current level of asthma control can be easily assessed by validated instruments, but it is currently difficult to assess individuals' level of future risk.
29936188|ab|2|29936188|OBJECTIVE|OBJECTIVE|OBJECTIVE|Develop, and validate, a risk prediction score for level of future risk, including patient characteristics and information on early treatment response.
29936188|ab|3|29936188|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|We used data of 304 adult patients with asthma from a 12-month primary care randomized controlled trial with 3-monthly assessments.
29936188|ab|4|29936188|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|With logistic regression we modeled the association between the level of future risk and patient characteristics including early treatment response.
29936188|ab|5|29936188|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|Future risk was defined as Asthma Control Questionnaire (ACQ) score of 1.5 or more at 12 months or the experience of at least 1 exacerbation during the final 6 months.
29936188|ab|6|29936188|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|We developed a risk prediction score on the basis of regression coefficients.
29936188|ab|7|29936188|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Performance of the risk prediction score improved, taking into account data on early treatment response (area under receiver-operating curve [AUROC] = 0.84) compared with a model containing only baseline characteristics (AUROC = 0.78).
29936188|ab|8|29936188|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|The score includes 6 easy-to-obtain predictors: sex, ACQ score and exacerbations in the previous year at baseline and at first follow-up, and smoking status and exacerbations in the previous 3 months (indicating early treatment response).
29936188|ab|9|29936188|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|External validation yielded an AUROC of 0.77.
29936188|ab|10|29936188|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|The risk prediction score classified patients into 3 risk groups: low (absolute risk, 11.7%), intermediate (47.0%), and high (72.7%).
29936188|ab|11|29936188|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|We developed and externally validated a risk prediction score, quantifying both level of current asthma control and the guideline-defined future risk.
29936188|ab|12|29936188|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|Patients' individual risk can now be estimated in an easy way, as proposed but not specified, by asthma management guidelines.

29897822|ab|14|29897822|CONCLUSION|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|Similar energy compensation occurred in response to1500 kcal/week and 3000 kcal/week of exercise energy expenditure.
29897822|ab|15|29897822|CONCLUSION|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|Exercise energy expenditure of 3000 kcal/week is great enough to exceed compensatory responses and reduce fat mass.

29877740|ab|3|29877740|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|Randomly-selected adults (N=964) with a history of physician-diagnosed asthma were studied from 2005-2007 and from 2012-2016.

29877740|ab|7|29877740|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Between-visit absolute variability in FEV1 was significantly greater in those in whom current asthma was confirmed, compared to those in whom current asthma was ruled out (7.3% vs 4.8%, mean difference between the 2 groups = 2.5%; 95% CI: 1.7-3.3%).
29877740|ab|8|29877740|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|However, a 12 percent and 200 mL between-visit variation in FEV1, which is the diagnostic threshold recommended by GINA, exhibited a sensitivity of only 0.17 and a specificity of 0.94 for confirming current asthma.

29949044|ab|7|29949044|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|The investigation group demonstrated a marked decrease in the frequency of the critical error of maintaining a slow inhalation rate until the lungs are full-a technique difficult to learn via verbal counselling alone.

29948069|ab|2|29948069|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|In 32 patients with a benign or malignant bone lesion (mean age 33.9 +/- 18.5 years, 17 females), 3-T MR imaging was performed including a 3D T1-weighted gradient echo sequence as the basis for the CT-like images.
29948069|ab|3|29948069|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|From these, intensity-inverted MR image volumes were converted into 2D images via a forward projection to obtain simulated radiographs.
29948069|ab|4|29948069|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|Two radiologists assessed these images as well as conventional radiographs for the type of periosteal reaction, matrix mineralization and destruction pattern.
29948069|ab|5|29948069|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|Agreement between the modalities was calculated using Cohen's kappa.
29948069|ab|6|29948069|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|The agreement between conventional radiographs and MR-derived CT-like images in combination with simulated radiographs was substantial (periosteal reaction, kappa = 0.67; destruction pattern, kappa = 0.75), and the sensitivity of both modalities for the final diagnosis of the lesion (aggressive vs. nonaggressive) was high (MR-derived CT-like images, 86.2% vs. conventional radiographs, 90.0%).
29948069|ab|7|29948069|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Additional information on soft tissue extension (MR-derived CT-like images, 21.9% vs. conventional radiographs, 12.5%; p = 0.009) and lobulation (9.4% vs. 0%; p < 0.001) was significantly more often found on MR-derived CT-like images compared with conventional radiographs.
29948069|ab|8|29948069|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|The assessment of the destruction patterns, periosteal reaction and distinction between aggressive and nonaggressive tumors was feasible using MR-derived CT-like images and simulated radiographs and is comparable to that of conventional radiographs.

21423523|ab|2|21423523||BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|For more than a decade, this spike-timing-dependent plasticity (STDP) has been studied mainly in brain slices of different brain structures and cultured neurons.

21423523|ab|6|21423523||CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|In spite of the ubiquity of STDP phenomena, a number of significant variations of the rule are observed in different structures, neuronal types and even synapses on the same neuron, as well as between in vitro and in vivo conditions.
21423523|ab|7|21423523||CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|In addition, the state of the neuronal network, its ongoing activity and the activation of ascending neuromodulatory systems in different behavioral conditions have dramatic consequences on the expression of spike-timing-dependent synaptic plasticity, and should be further explored.
