21325707|ab|1|21325707||BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|In computed tomography there are different situations where reconstruction has to be performed with limited raw data.
21325707|ab|2|21325707||BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|In the past few years it has been shown that algorithms which are based on compressed sensing theory are able to handle incomplete datasets quite well.
21325707|ab|3|21325707||BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|As a cost function these algorithms use the l(1)-norm of the image after it has been transformed by a sparsifying transformation.
21325707|ab|4|21325707||OBJECTIVE|BACKGROUND|This yields to an inequality-constrained convex optimization problem.
21325707|ab|5|21325707||BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|Due to the large size of the optimization problem some heuristic optimization algorithms have been proposed in the past few years.
21325707|ab|6|21325707||BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|The most popular way is optimizing the raw data and sparsity cost functions separately in an alternating manner.
21325707|ab|7|21325707||OBJECTIVE|OBJECTIVE|In this paper we will follow this strategy and present a new method to adapt these optimization steps.
21325707|ab|8|21325707||RESULTS|METHODS|Compared to existing methods which perform similarly, the proposed method needs no a priori knowledge about the raw data consistency.
21325707|ab|9|21325707||RESULTS|METHODS|It is ensured that the algorithm converges to the lowest possible value of the raw data cost function, while holding the sparsity constraint at a low value.
21325707|ab|10|21325707||METHODS|METHODS|This is achieved by transferring the step-size determination of both optimization procedures into the raw data domain, where they are adapted to each other.
21325707|ab|11|21325707||METHODS|METHODS|To evaluate the algorithm, we process measured clinical datasets.
21325707|ab|12|21325707||METHODS|METHODS|To cover a wide field of possible applications, we focus on the problems of angular undersampling, data lost due to metal implants, limited view angle tomography and interior tomography.
21325707|ab|13|21325707||RESULTS|RESULTS|In all cases the presented method reaches convergence within less than 25 iteration steps, while using a constant set of algorithm control parameters.
21325707|ab|14|21325707||RESULTS|RESULTS|The image artifacts caused by incomplete raw data are mostly removed without introducing new effects like staircasing.
21325707|ab|15|21325707||CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|All scenarios are compared to an existing implementation of the ASD-POCS algorithm, which realizes the step-size adaption in a different way.
21325707|ab|16|21325707||CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|Additional prior information as proposed by the PICCS algorithm can be incorporated easily into the optimization process.

23589619|ab|1|23589619||BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|Lysis of RBCs during numerous clinical settings such as severe hemolytic anemia, infection, tissue injury, or blood transfusion releases the endogenous damage-associated molecular pattern, hemoglobin (Hb), into the plasma.
23589619|ab|2|23589619||BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|The redox-reactive Hb generates cytotoxic reactive oxygen species, disrupting the redox balance and impairing the immune-responsive blood cells.
23589619|ab|3|23589619||BACKGROUND|OBJECTIVE|Therefore, it is crucial to understand how the immune system defends against the cytotoxic Hb.
23589619|ab|4|23589619||OBJECTIVE|RESULTS|We identified a shortcut "capture and quench" mechanism of detoxification of Hb by the monocyte scavenger receptor CD163, independent of the well-known dominant antioxidant, haptoglobin.
23589619|ab|5|23589619||RESULTS|RESULTS|Our findings support a highly efficient two-pass mechanism of detoxification and clearance of Hb: 1) a direct suppression of Hb-pseudoperoxidase activity by CD163, involving an autocrine loop of CD163 shedding, sequestration of Hb, recycling, and homeostasis of CD163 in human monocytes and 2) paracrine transactivation of endothelial cells by the shedded soluble CD163 (sCD163), which further detoxifies and clears residual Hb.
23589619|ab|6|23589619||RESULTS|RESULTS|We showed that sCD163 and IgG interact with free Hb in the plasma and subsequently the sCD163-Hb-IgG complex is endocytosed into monocytes via FcgammaR.
23589619|ab|7|23589619||RESULTS|RESULTS|The endocytosed sCD163 is recycled to restore the homeostasis of CD163 on the monocyte membrane in an autocrine cycle, whereas the internalized Hb is catabolized.
23589619|ab|8|23589619||RESULTS|RESULTS|Using ex vivo coculture experiments, we demonstrated that the monocyte-derived sCD163 and IgG shuttle residual plasma Hb into the proximal endothelial cells.
23589619|ab|9|23589619||CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|These findings suggest that CD163 and IgG collaborate to engage monocytes and endothelial cells in a two-pass detoxification mechanism to mount a systemic defense against Hb-induced oxidative stress.

29952676|ab|3|29952676|CONTEXT|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|The effects of galangin on hyperglycaemia and lipid abnormalities are not known.
29952676|ab|4|29952676|OBJECTIVE|OBJECTIVE|OBJECTIVE|To elucidate the effectiveness of galangin on hyperglycaemia-associated complications and lipid changes in rats with streptozotocin (STZ)-induced hyperglycaemia.
29952676|ab|5|29952676|OBJECTIVE|OBJECTIVE|METHODS|Diabetes was induced in adult Wistar rats by administering 40 mg/kg of STZ.

29952676|ab|7|29952676|OBJECTIVE|OBJECTIVE|METHODS|Therefore three doses of galangin (4, 8 or 16 mg/kg BW) or glibenclamide (600 microg/kg BW) were administered daily to diabetic rats orally for 45 days.
29952676|ab|8|29952676|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Diabetic rats showed a significant (p < 0.05) increased levels of plasma glucose (281.10 mg/dL) and decreased levels of insulin (6.01 muU/mL).

29952676|ab|10|29952676|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|When galangin was administered to the hyperglycaemic rats, plasma glucose and insulin levels and lipid profiles reverted to levels similar to those in healthy control rats.
29952676|ab|11|29952676|DISCUSSION AND CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|Administration of galangin reduced hyperlipidaemia related to the risk of diabetic complications and could be beneficial for diabetic hyperlipidaemic patients.
29952676|ab|12|29952676|DISCUSSION AND CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|Further work detailing its mechanism-of-action for improving hyperglycaemic-associated lipid abnormalities is needed.

29921540|ab|5|29921540|MAIN OUTCOME MEASURES|METHODS|METHODS|Participants completed a validated survey measuring food insecurity (six-item US Food Security Survey Module), self-care capacity (Self-Care Capacity Scale), depressive symptoms (10-item Geriatric Depression Scale), and nutritional status (Mini Nutritional Assessment Short-Form).
29921540|ab|6|29921540|STATISTICAL ANALYSES PERFORMED|METHODS|METHODS|Generalized structural equation modeling was used to include the simultaneous equations and multiple mediators in one model.
29921540|ab|7|29921540|STATISTICAL ANALYSES PERFORMED|METHODS|METHODS|The Akaike Information Criterion, Bayesian Information Criterion, and likelihood ratio tests were conducted to compare the fit of competing model specifications.

29921540|ab|12|29921540|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Although food insecurity was not significantly associated with nutritional status, a significant indirect association between food insecurity and nutritional status through depressive symptoms was observed (b=.02, P=0.04).
29921540|ab|13|29921540|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|Study results indicate functionally impaired low-income older adults encounter greater food insecurity.
29921540|ab|14|29921540|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|Inability to afford food combined with limited ability to take care of oneself contributes to an increased self-report of depressive symptoms, resulting in less favorable nutritional status.

29954636|ab|1|29954636|OBJECTIVE|OBJECTIVE|BACKGROUND|Previous studies have shown that a subgroup of children with suspected (central) auditory processing disorder (SusCAPD) have insufficient ability to use binaural cues to benefit from spatial processing.
29954636|ab|2|29954636|OBJECTIVE|OBJECTIVE|BACKGROUND|Thus, they experience considerable listening difficulties in challenging auditory environments, such as classrooms.
29954636|ab|3|29954636|OBJECTIVE|OBJECTIVE|BACKGROUND|Some researchers have also indicated the probable role of binaural temporal fine structure (TFS) in the perceptual segregation of target signal from noise and hence in speech perception in noise.
29954636|ab|4|29954636|OBJECTIVE|OBJECTIVE|OBJECTIVE|Therefore, in the present study, in order to further investigate the underlying reason for listening problems against background noise in this group of children, their performance was measured using binaural TFS sensitivity test (TFS-LF) as well as behavioral auditory lateralization in noise test, both of which are based on binaural temporal cues processing.
29954636|ab|5|29954636|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|Participants in this analytical study included 91 children with normal hearing and no listening problems and 41 children (9-12 years old) with SusCAPD who found it challenging to understand speech in noise.
29954636|ab|6|29954636|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|Initially, the ability to use binaural TFS was measured at three frequencies (250, 500 and 750Hz) in both the groups, and the results of preliminary evaluations were compared between normal children and those with SusCAPD who participated in the study.
29954636|ab|7|29954636|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|Thereafter, the binaural performance of the 16 children with SusCAPD who had higher thresholds than the normal group at all three frequencies tested in TFS-LF test was examined using the lateralization test in 7 spatial locations.
29954636|ab|8|29954636|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Total 16 of the 41 children with SusCAPD who participated in this study (39%) showed poor performance on the TFS-LF test at all three frequencies, compared to both normal children and other children in the APD group (p<0.05).
29954636|ab|9|29954636|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Furthermore, children in the APD group with binaural TFS coding deficits at all three frequencies revealed significant differences in the lateralization test results compared to normal children (p<0.05).
29954636|ab|10|29954636|CONCLUSION|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|Findings of the current study demonstrated that one of the underlying causes for the difficulty understanding speech in noisy environments experienced by a subgroup of children with SusCAPD can be the reduced ability to benefit from binaural TFS information.
29954636|ab|11|29954636|CONCLUSION|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|This study also showed that a reduced ability to use binaural TFS cues in the group of children with SusCAPD was accompanied by reduced binaural processing abilities in the lateralization test which also admit the presence of binaural temporal processing deficits in this group of children.

29948065|ab|6|29948065|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Wall thickening, circumferential and radial strain were all significantly diminished in segments with hyperenhancement and decreased even further if MVO was also present (all p < 0.001).

29906201|ab|3|29906201|METHOD|METHODS|METHODS|Second-by-second symbolic representations were created of each team member's electroencephalographic power, and quantitative estimates of their neurodynamic organizations were calculated from the Shannon entropy of the symbolic data streams.
29906201|ab|4|29906201|METHOD|METHODS|METHODS|The information in the neurodynamic data streams of health care ( n = 24), submarine navigation ( n = 12), and high school problem-solving ( n = 13) dyads was separated into the information of each team member, the information shared by team members, and the overall team information.
29906201|ab|5|29906201|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Most of the team information was the sum of each individual's neurodynamic information.
29906201|ab|6|29906201|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|The remaining team information was shared among the team members.
29906201|ab|7|29906201|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|This shared information averaged ~15% of the individual information, with momentary levels of 1% to 80%.
29906201|ab|8|29906201|CONCLUSION|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|Continuous quantitative estimates can be made from the shared, individual, and team neurodynamic information about the contributions of different team members to the overall neurodynamic organization of a team and the neurodynamic interdependencies among the team members.

29932740|ab|7|29932740|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|We use a psychophysical estimation of Just Noticeable Differences in Level (JNDL) for vertical vibration transmitted to cyclists on a road simulator.
29932740|ab|8|29932740|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|In Experiment 1, we estimate the JNDL for whole-body vibration using vertical excitation on both wheels simultaneously (20 male cyclists).
29932740|ab|9|29932740|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|In Experiment 2, we estimate the JNDL at two different points of contact by applying the same signal to only the hands or the buttocks (9 male cyclists).

29932740|ab|12|29932740|CONCLUSION|CONCLUSIONS|RESULTS|Using these two metrics and at all points of contact, vibration magnitude needs to be reduced by at least 15%, for the change to be detectable by road cyclists.
29932740|ab|13|29932740|APPLICATION|CONCLUSIONS|RESULTS|A road bicycle needs to transmit at least 15% less vibration for male cyclists to detect an improvement in dynamic comfort.
29932740|ab|14|29932740|APPLICATION|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|Dynamic bicycle comfort can be measured in terms of a new metric: power transmitted to the cyclist.

29883939|ab|1|29883939|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|Humans alter gait in response to unusual gait circumstances to accomplish the task of walking.
29883939|ab|2|29883939|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|For instance, subjects spontaneously increase leg compliance at a step length threshold as step length increases.
29883939|ab|3|29883939|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|OBJECTIVE|Here we test the hypothesis that this transition occurs based on the level of energy expenditure, where compliant walking becomes less energetically demanding at long step lengths.
29883939|ab|4|29883939|RESEARCH QUESTION|OBJECTIVE|OBJECTIVE|To map and compare the metabolic cost of normal and compliant walking as step length increases.
29883939|ab|5|29883939|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|10 healthy individuals walked on a treadmill using progressively increasing step lengths (100%, 120%, 140% and 160% of preferred step length), in both normal and compliant leg walking as energy expenditure was recorded via indirect calorimetry.
29883939|ab|6|29883939|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|Leg compliance was controlled by lowering the center-of-mass trajectory during stance, forcing the leg to flex and extend as the body moved over the foot contact.
29883939|ab|7|29883939|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|For normal step lengths, compliant leg walking was more costly than normal walking gait, but compliant leg walking energetic cost did not increase as rapidly for longer step lengths.
29883939|ab|8|29883939|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|This led to an intersection between normal and compliant walking cost curves at 114% relative step length (regression analysis; r(2)=0.92 for normal walking; r(2)=0.65 for compliant walking).
29883939|ab|9|29883939|SIGNIFICANCE|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|Compliant leg walking is less energetically demanding at longer step lengths where a spontaneous shift to compliant walking has been observed, suggesting the human motor control system is sensitive to energetic requirements and will employ alternate movement patterns if advantageous strategies are available.
29883939|ab|10|29883939|SIGNIFICANCE|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|The transition could be attributed to the interplay between (i) leg work controlling body travel during single stance and (ii) leg work to control energy loss in the step-to-step transition.
29883939|ab|11|29883939|SIGNIFICANCE|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|Compliant leg walking requires more stance leg work at normal step lengths, but involves less energy loss at the step-to-step transition for very long steps.

17498590|ab|1|17498590||OBJECTIVE|OBJECTIVE|To test the hypothesis of whether cellular blue nevi (CBN) may originate from "ordinary" compound and dermal nevi, a total of 275 melanocytic nevi including 59 CBN, 34 ordinary blue nevi, 87 combined nevi (including 43 so-called clonal nevi), 35 deep penetrating nevi, and 60 ordinary compound and dermal nevi (30 of each) were studied for the presence of so-called ball-in-mitts and microalveolar structures.
17498590|ab|2|17498590||METHODS|METHODS|A ball-in-mitts structure was defined as a single centrally placed melanocyte with a round to oval nucleus (the "ball" cell) and a clear, dusty, or pigmented cytoplasm encircled by a single dendritic cell (the "mitt" cell) with an oval to spindle-shaped nucleus and slender bipolar processes containing melanin and surrounding at least one fourth of the ball's diameter.
17498590|ab|3|17498590||METHODS|METHODS|A microalveolar structure was defined as a group of 2 to 10 centrally placed melanocytes with round to oval nuclei and clear, dusty, or pigmented cytoplasm (balls) surrounded by one or more cells (mitts) with spindle-shaped nuclei and slender bipolar processes containing melanin.
17498590|ab|4|17498590||RESULTS|RESULTS|Microscopically, ball-in-mitt and microalveolar structures were detected in all types of nevi studied, with the highest incidence in combined nevi (82%), CBN (76%), and ordinary "nonblue" nevi (73%).
17498590|ab|5|17498590||RESULTS|RESULTS|In CBN, ball-in-mitts and microalveolar structures tended to be located in the deeper portion of the lesions, whereas in ordinary nonblue nevi, they were most often found superficially, just below the epidermis; in clonal nevi, these structures were often confined to the "clonal" parts.
17498590|ab|6|17498590||RESULTS|RESULTS|Immunohistochemically, ball-in-mitts and microalveolar structures were positive for HMB45.
17498590|ab|7|17498590||RESULTS|RESULTS|Ultrastructurally, the balls tended to have round to oval nuclei, whereas the mitts possessed oval, elongated to spindled nuclei.
17498590|ab|8|17498590||RESULTS|RESULTS|Melanosomes were found in various stages in the cells of both structures.
17498590|ab|9|17498590||RESULTS|RESULTS|The cytoplasm of the mitts typically formed elongated polar processes, sometimes with club-like widenings at the ends, completely or partially encircling the balls.
17498590|ab|10|17498590||RESULTS|RESULTS|In the microalveolar structures, the adjacent cells forming the mitts surrounded the ball cells like a chain.
17498590|ab|11|17498590||CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|Our study suggests that some or even most cases of CBN may evolve from ordinary nonblue nevi.
17498590|ab|12|17498590||CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|This process may involve several steps and is probably reflected by the appearances of combined nevi, deep penetrating nevi, and CBN.
17498590|ab|13|17498590||CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|These nevi often show a morphological overlap, and ball-in-mitts and microalveolar structures found in various stages of their development seem to greatly account for this overlap.

29952710|ab|1|29952710|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|Psoriasis is a chronic, hyper-proliferative dermatological condition associated with joint symptoms known as psoriatic arthritis (PsA).
29952710|ab|2|29952710|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|In a 2013 review, the total economic burden of PsA was estimated at $51.7-$63.2 billion.
29952710|ab|3|29952710|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|The economic burden of moderate to severe psoriasis patients has reduced significantly with the advent of biologics, but there remains a dearth of real-world evidence of the impact of treatment persistence on the economic burden of moderate to severe psoriasis and/or PsA patients.
29952710|ab|4|29952710|OBJECTIVE|OBJECTIVE|OBJECTIVE|To evaluate the overall and psoriasis and/or PsA-related health care utilization and costs among patients who were persistent versus those nonpersistent on index biologic among the moderate to severe psoriasis and/or PsA population.
29952710|ab|5|29952710|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|Adult patients with >/= 2 claims with diagnosis of psoriasis and/or PsA during the period of November 2010-October 2015 were identified from the U.S.
29952710|ab|6|29952710|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|Department of Defense database; the first diagnosis date during November 2011-October 2014 was defined as the index date.
29952710|ab|7|29952710|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|As of the index date, patients were considered to have moderate to severe psoriasis or PsA if they had >/= 1 nontopical systemic therapy or phototherapy during the 1-year pre- or 1-month post-index date.
29952710|ab|8|29952710|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|Persistence to index therapy, defined as the first biologic used (etanercept, adalimumab, ustekinumab, infliximab) on or within 30 days post-index date, was determined based on the biologic dosing schedule and a 90-day gap.
29952710|ab|9|29952710|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|Generalized linear models were used to compare the health care utilization and costs between persistent and nonpersistent patients during the 1-year post-index period.
29952710|ab|10|29952710|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|A total of 2,945 moderate to severe psoriasis and/or PsA patients were identified.

29952710|ab|12|29952710|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Compared with nonpersistent patients, persistent patients were older (49.2 vs. 45.5 years; P < 0.001) and more likely to be male (52% vs. 45%; P < 0.001).
29952710|ab|13|29952710|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|More persistent patients were diagnosed with dyslipidemia (40% vs. 35%; P = 0.002), had lower antidepressant use (23.4% vs. 27.4%; P < 0.001), and had lower anxiolytic use (30% vs. 37%; P < 0.001) compared with nonpersistent patients.
29952710|ab|14|29952710|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|After adjusting for demographic and clinical characteristics, nonpersistent patients had higher total medical costs ($12,457 vs. $8,964; P < 0.001) compared with persistent patients, and ambulatory visits (23.9 vs. 21.4; P = 0.007) were a major contributor.
29952710|ab|15|29952710|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Approximately 40% of the total overall medical costs were attributed to psoriasis and PsA.
29952710|ab|16|29952710|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Although persistent patients incurred higher pharmacy costs ($10,684 vs. $7,849; P < 0.001) due to higher biologic use and the potentially high per-unit cost of biologics, their psoriasis- and/or PsA-related medical costs were significantly lower than those of nonpersistent patients ($3,395 vs. $5,041; P < 0.001).
29952710|ab|17|29952710|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Total overall costs combining medical and pharmacy costs were similar between the cohorts ($22,678 vs. $21,477; P = 0.122).
29952710|ab|18|29952710|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|Moderate to severe psoriasis and/or PsA patients who were persistent on index biologic treatment had higher pharmacy utilization and costs, albeit with lower medical costs and similar total costs, compared with nonpersistent patients.

29895513|ab|1|29895513|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|Cognitive biases refer to automatic attentional and interpretational tendencies, which could be retained by cognitive bias modification interventions.
29895513|ab|2|29895513|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|Cristea et al and Jones et al have published reviews (in 2016 and 2017 respectively) on the effectiveness of such interventions.
29895513|ab|3|29895513|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|The advancement of technologies such as electronic health (eHealth) and mobile health (mHealth) has led to them being harnessed for the delivery of cognitive bias modification.
29895513|ab|4|29895513|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|To date, at least eight studies have demonstrated the feasibility of mobile technologies for the delivery of cognitive bias modification.

29895513|ab|7|29895513|OBJECTIVE|OBJECTIVE|OBJECTIVE|It is important to have a common platform that could facilitate the design and customization of cognitive bias modification interventions for a variety of psychiatric and addictive disorders.
29895513|ab|8|29895513|OBJECTIVE|OBJECTIVE|OBJECTIVE|It is the aim of the current research protocol to describe the design of a research platform that allows for customization of cognitive bias modification interventions for addictive disorders.

29895513|ab|10|29895513|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|The proposed platform would comprise of a mobile phone version of the cognitive bias task which is controlled by a server that could customize the algorithm for the tasks and collate the reaction-time data in realtime.

29956092|ab|3|29956092|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|Six breast quality measures were analyzed using the National Cancer Data Base from 2014 to 2015, and a multivariable model was used to assess performance for each measure by region.
29956092|ab|4|29956092|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|Kaplan-Meier and Cox proportional hazard models were used to examine OS between high- and low-performing centers from 2007 to 2012.
29956092|ab|5|29956092|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Overall, 305,391 women had surgery at 1322 institutions in nine US regions; 90.8% underwent needle biopsy (range 86.0-92.6% between regions, p < 0.01), 69.8% had breast-conserving surgery (BCS) for stage 0-II cancer (60.9-79.3%, p < 0.01), 85.2% aged < 70 years had radiation therapy (RT) after BCS (79.6-90.8%, p < 0.01), 78.3% of women with four or more positive nodes had post-mastectomy RT (70.9-84.5%, p < 0.01), 90.9% with hormone receptor (HR)-positive stage IB-III cancer had hormone therapy (83.7-95.1%, p < 0.01), and 89.4% aged < 70 years with HR-negative stage IB-III cancer had chemotherapy (87.6-91.4%, p < 0.01).
29956092|ab|6|29956092|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Multivariate analyses adjusted for patient and facility factors found that region was the only consistent predictor of non-compliance across measures.
29956092|ab|7|29956092|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|With median 65-month follow-up, there was no difference in OS between high- and low-performing centers for the three measures that have been shown to impact OS.
29956092|ab|8|29956092|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|There is significant regional variation in performance on the breast quality measures but this variation did not impact OS.
29956092|ab|9|29956092|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|Targeted efforts in certain areas of the country may help improve performance on these measures.
22198709|ab|1|22198709||BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|Many dental bleaching techniques are now available, several of them using a laser source.
22198709|ab|2|22198709||BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|However, the literature on the exact role of coherent light in the biochemical reaction of the whitening process is very discordant.
22198709|ab|3|22198709||OBJECTIVE|OBJECTIVE|The aims of this in vitro study were: (1) to compare two different laser sources, a KTP laser with a wavelength of 532 nm and a diode laser with a wavelength of 808 nm, during dental bleaching, and (2) to investigate the relationships among changes in gel temperature, tooth shade and hydrogen peroxide (HP) concentration during laser irradiation.
22198709|ab|4|22198709||METHODS|METHODS|Altogether, 116 bovine teeth were bleached using a 30% HP gel, some of them with gel only and others with gel plus one of the two lasers (532 or 808 nm) at two different powers (2 and 4 W).
22198709|ab|5|22198709||METHODS|METHODS|The KTP laser produced a significant shade variation with a minimal temperature increase.
22198709|ab|6|22198709||RESULTS|RESULTS|The diode laser led to a higher temperature increase with a greater reduction in HP concentration, but the change in shade was only statistically significant with a power of 4 W.
22198709|ab|7|22198709||RESULTS|RESULTS|At a power of 2 W, the KTP laser caused a greater change in shade than the diode laser.
22198709|ab|8|22198709||RESULTS|RESULTS|No significant correlations were found among temperature, HP concentration and shade variation.
22198709|ab|9|22198709||CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|The KTP laser appears to provide better results with less dangerous thermal increases than the diode laser.
22198709|ab|10|22198709||CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|This might call into question most of the literature affirming that the action of laser bleaching is by increasing the gel temperature and, consequently, the speed of the redox reaction.
22198709|ab|11|22198709||CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|Further study is required to investigate the correlations between the parameters investigated and efficacy of the bleaching process.

29957307|ab|1|29957307|INTRODUCTION|BACKGROUND|OBJECTIVE|The 2-fold purpose of this study was to evaluate the effects of acid etching and calcium chloride immersion on removal torque and the bone-cutting ability of orthodontic mini-implants (OMIs).
29957307|ab|2|29957307|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|For the removal torque part of the study, 3 types of OMIs (titanium alloy) were evaluated in a rabbit model: OMIs with acid surface etching with and without calcium chloride immersion (ECG and EG, respectively) and a control group (CG), in which the OMIs had an untreated, machined surface.
29957307|ab|3|29957307|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|We inserted 126 OMIs (42 OMIs per type) into both tibias of 21 male rabbits (5 months of age) with body weights of 3.0 to 3.5 kg.
29957307|ab|4|29957307|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|Removal torque was evaluated after 1, 4, and 7 weeks.
29957307|ab|5|29957307|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|To determine the OMIs' bone-cutting ability, total insertion time to place an OMI 6 mm into artificial bone was measured (6 OMIs per group).
29957307|ab|6|29957307|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Removal torque values for the EG (3.97 +/- 0.52 Ncm) and ECG (4.21 +/- 0.44 Ncm) were statistically and significantly higher than those of the CG (3.02 +/- 0.53 Ncm) 1 week after implantation (P <0.05).
29957307|ab|7|29957307|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|The ECG (6.54 +/- 0.50, 6.61 +/- 0.66 Ncm) showed the highest removal torque value followed by the EG (5.68 +/- 0.58, 5.89 +/- 0.70 Ncm) and CG (3.43 +/- 0.62, 3.38 +/- 0.54 Ncm) at 4 and 7 weeks after implantation (P <0.05).
29957307|ab|8|29957307|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Removal torque did not change over time with the CG, but with the ECG and EG, it was significantly higher in weeks 4 and 7 than in week 1 (P <0.05).
29957307|ab|9|29957307|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Total insertion time was significantly greater for the EG than for the ECG and CG (P <0.05).
29957307|ab|10|29957307|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|Treating OMIs with a calcium chloride solution improved the initial bone reaction by preventing contamination of the implant surface, and increasing the surface roughness of OMIs by acid etching enhanced their stability without decreasing the bone-cutting ability compared with OMIs without surface treatment.

29953302|ab|4|29953302|MATERIALS AND METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|The pharmacokinetic profiles of losartan and EXP3174 of orally administered losartan (10 mg/kg) with or without GLT pretreatment (80 mg/kg/day for 10 days) in Sprague-Dawley rats were determined.

29953302|ab|9|29953302|DISCUSSION AND CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|The results indicate that GLT might increase the plasma concentration of losartan and decrease the concentration of EXP3174 through inhibiting the metabolism of losartan.

29958226|ab|2|29958226|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|In McGrath videolaryngoscopic intubation, lifting of the blade to raise the epiglottis is needed to visualize the glottis, but in patients with an unstable cervical spine, this can cause cervical spine movement.

29958226|ab|4|29958226|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|OBJECTIVE|We therefore hypothesized that the Optiscope would produce less cervical spine movement than the McGrath videolaryngoscope during tracheal intubation.

29958226|ab|6|29958226|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|The primary outcome of the study was the extent of cervical spine motion at the occiput-C1, C1-C2, and C2-C5 segments.
29958226|ab|7|29958226|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|In this randomized crossover study, the cervical spine angle was measured before and during tracheal intubation using either the Optiscope or the McGrath videolaryngoscope in 21 patients with simulated cervical immobilization.
29958226|ab|8|29958226|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|Cervical spine motion was defined as the change in angle at each cervical segment during tracheal intubation.
29958226|ab|9|29958226|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|There was significantly less cervical spine motion at the occiput-C1 segment using the Optiscope rather than the McGrath videolaryngoscope (mean [98.33% CI]: 4.7 degrees [2.4-7.0] vs 10.4 degrees [8.1-12.7]; mean difference [98.33% CI]: -5.7 degrees [-7.5 to -3.9]).
29958226|ab|10|29958226|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|There were also fewer cervical spinal motions at the C1-C2 and C2-C5 segments using the Optiscope (mean difference versus the McGrath videolaryngoscope [98.33% CI]: -2.4 degrees [-3.7 to -1.2]) and -3.7 degrees [-5.9 to -1.4], respectively).
29958226|ab|11|29958226|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|The Optiscope produces less cervical spine motion than the McGrath videolaryngoscope during tracheal intubation of patients with simulated cervical immobilization.

29941296|ab|8|29941296|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Those patients who were randomly assigned to risperidone had higher levels of IL-8 (p=0.000) and MIP-1beta (p=0.007) than healthy volunteers at baseline, whereas no differences were found between patients initially assigned to aripiprazole and healthy volunteers.
29941296|ab|9|29941296|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Three months following the onset of medication several cytokines decreased significantly: IL-8, MIP-1beta, Fractalkine, TNF-alpha, IL-7, IL-13, IL-17alpha, IL-23, IL-21 (all ps<0.01).
29941296|ab|10|29941296|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|No differences were found in the percentages of change between both treatments.
29941296|ab|11|29941296|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|The effect size of the two antipsychotics was similar, except for TNF-alpha, IL-13, IL-17alpha and Fractalkine, in which aripiprazole seems to have a greater effect size than risperidone, whereas risperidone seems to have a greater effect size than aripiprazole on MIP-1beta.
29941296|ab|12|29941296|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|This is the first study that has compared the immunomodulatory effect of risperidone and aripiprazole, finding that the anti-inflammatory effect of both treatments was similar.

29954455|ab|2|29954455|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|Because it is a benign tumor, it does not require radiotherapy, chemotherapy, or extensive resection.

29954455|ab|6|29954455|CASE PRESENTATION|METHODS|METHODS|A 39-year-old man presented to a local clinic with a 1-month history of a painless mass in his left neck.
29954455|ab|7|29954455|CASE PRESENTATION|METHODS|METHODS|Results of a needle biopsy suggested an atypical lipomatous tumor, and the patient was referred to our hospital.
29954455|ab|8|29954455|CASE PRESENTATION|METHODS|METHODS|Physical examination revealed a hard and mobile mass in the left neck.
29954455|ab|9|29954455|CASE PRESENTATION|METHODS|METHODS|Plain X-ray radiographs showed an absence of calcification in the soft tissue mass.
29954455|ab|10|29954455|CASE PRESENTATION|METHODS|METHODS|MRI revealed a well-defined and lobulated mass, and on T1-weighted images, the lesion showed heterogeneity, with higher signal intensity than that of muscle.
29954455|ab|11|29954455|CASE PRESENTATION|METHODS|METHODS|On T2-weighted images, the septum had low-signal intensity.

29954455|ab|13|29954455|CASE PRESENTATION|METHODS|METHODS|The SUVmax of the mass on FDG PET was 1.84.

29954455|ab|15|29954455|CASE PRESENTATION|METHODS|METHODS|The mass was resected marginally.

29954455|ab|19|29954455|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|Chondroid lipoma is an extremely rare benign soft tissue tumor that is often confused with sarcoma.
29954455|ab|20|29954455|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|It is very important to differentiate chondroid lipoma from sarcoma when the SUVmax value of the mass is low, even when biopsy results suggest that it is a sarcoma.

29903344|ab|5|29903344|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|From June 2006 through October 2009, 375 patients with 1 or more thromboembolic risk factors were also randomized to lower intensity warfarin plus aspirin (international normalized ratio 1.5 to 2.0; n = 185) or standard warfarin plus aspirin (international normalized ratio 2.0 to 3.0; n = 190) 3 months after mAVR (high-risk arm).
29903344|ab|6|29903344|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|The low-risk arm was terminated for excess cerebral thromboembolic events (3.12% per patient-year vs. 0.29% per patient-year, p = 0.02) in the DAPT group at up to 8.8-year follow-up (631.6 patient-years), with no differences in bleeding or all-cause mortality.

29903344|ab|9|29903344|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|International normalized ratios were safely maintained at 1.5 to 2.0 in high-risk patients, without differences in mortality or thromboembolic complications.

29954409|ab|1|29954409|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|Implementation is proposed to be a multiphase, multilevel process.
29954409|ab|2|29954409|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|After a period of exploration, an adoption decision is made, typically at the upper management or policy level.
29954409|ab|3|29954409|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|Nevertheless, movement through each of the subsequent phases of the implementation process involves clinicians or providers at the individual level to adopt the innovation and then change their behavior to use/deliver the innovation.
29954409|ab|4|29954409|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|Multiple behavioral change theories propose that intentions are a critical determinant of implementation behavior.
29954409|ab|5|29954409|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|However, there is a need for the development and testing of pragmatic measures of providers' intentions to use a specific innovation or evidence-based practice (EBP).
29954409|ab|6|29954409|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|Nine items were developed to assess providers' intentions to use a specific innovation or EBP.
29954409|ab|7|29954409|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|Motivational interviewing was the EBP in the study.
29954409|ab|8|29954409|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|Items were administered, as part of larger survey, to 179 providers across 38 substance use disorder treatment (SUDT) programs within five agencies in California, USA.
29954409|ab|9|29954409|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|Rasch analysis was conducted using RUMM2030 software to assess the items, their overall fit to the Rasch model, the response scale used, individual item fit, differential item functioning (DIF), and person separation.
29954409|ab|10|29954409|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Following a stepwise process, the scale was reduced from nine items to three items to increase the feasibility and acceptability of the scale while maintaining suitable psychometric properties.
29954409|ab|11|29954409|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|The three-item unidimensional scale showed good person separation (PSI = .872), no disordering of thresholds, and no evidence of uniform or non-uniform DIF.
29954409|ab|12|29954409|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Rasch analysis supported the viability of the scale as a measure of implementation intentions.
29954409|ab|13|29954409|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|The Measure of Innovation-Specific Implementation Intentions (MISII) is a sound measure of providers' intentions to use a specific innovation or EBP.
29954409|ab|14|29954409|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|Future evaluation of convergent, divergent, and predictive validity are needed.
29954409|ab|15|29954409|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|The study also demonstrates the value of Rasch analysis for testing the psychometric properties of pragmatic implementation measures.

29885870|ab|18|29885870|DISCUSSION|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|This study suggested that the underlining ureteral pathology lead to UVJ obstruction following Vantris injection.
29885870|ab|19|29885870|DISCUSSION|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|There was increased collagen deposition in the juxtavesical segment of the obstructive ureters following Vantris injection.
29885870|ab|20|29885870|DISCUSSION|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|Furthermore, these findings were similar to those discovered in patients who underwent endoscopic correction with Deflux, and in patients who required ureteral reimplantation due to primary obstructive megaureter.
29885870|ab|21|29885870|DISCUSSION|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|Additional biopsies from the muscularis propria adjacent to the injection site showed no significant abnormalities, ironing out the fact that Vantris did not led to adverse tissue reaction following injection.
29885870|ab|22|29885870|DISCUSSION|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|Univariate analysis further ironed out the hypothesis that underlying ureteral pathology was responsible for the increased incidence of UVJ obstruction and demonstrated that Grade V reflux, the presence of beak sign on the reviewed pretreatment VCUG, and inflamed bladder mucosa upon injection were significant independent risk factors leading to obstruction.
29885870|ab|23|29885870|CONCLUSION|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|Data showed that Vantris injection did not lead to any different ureteral fibrosis or inflammatory changes to the tissue augmenting substances utilized in past and present clinical practice, and therefore did not seem to increase the incidence of UVJ obstruction.
29885870|ab|24|29885870|CONCLUSION|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|High reflux grade, presence of obstructive/refluxing megaureter and inflamed bladder mucosa were the only statistically significant and independent predictive factors for UVJ obstruction following endoscopic correction of VUR.

29909877|ab|1|29909877|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|Empirical evidence supporting the cost-effectiveness estimates of particular health care technologies may be limited, or it may even be missing entirely.
29909877|ab|2|29909877|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|In these situations, additional information, often in the form of expert judgments, is needed to reach a decision.
29909877|ab|3|29909877|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|There are formal methods to quantify experts' beliefs, termed as structured expert elicitation (SEE), but only limited research is available in support of methodological choices.
29909877|ab|4|29909877|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|Perhaps as a consequence, the use of SEE in the context of cost-effectiveness modelling is limited.
29909877|ab|5|29909877|OBJECTIVES|OBJECTIVE|OBJECTIVE|This article reviews applications of SEE in cost-effectiveness modelling with the aim of summarizing the basis for methodological choices made in each application and recording the difficulties and challenges reported by the authors in the design, conduct, and analyses.
29909877|ab|6|29909877|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|The methods used in each application were extracted along with the criteria used to support methodological and practical choices and any issues or challenges discussed in the text.
29909877|ab|7|29909877|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|Issues and challenges were extracted using an open field, and then categorised and grouped for reporting.
29909877|ab|8|29909877|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|The review demonstrates considerable heterogeneity in methods used, and authors acknowledge great methodological uncertainty in justifying their choices.
29909877|ab|9|29909877|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Specificities of the context area emerging as potentially important in determining further methodological research in elicitation are between- expert variation and its interpretation, the fact that substantive experts in the area may not be trained in quantitative subjects, that judgments are often needed on various parameter types, the need for some form of assessment of validity, and the need for more integration with behavioural research to devise relevant debiasing strategies.
29909877|ab|10|29909877|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|This review of experiences of SEE highlights a number of specificities/constraints that can shape the development of guidance and target future research efforts in this area.

29957866|ab|2|29957866|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|BACKGROUND|Armed Forces' training and deployment have greatly increased, escalating the risk of injury and pain-related issues both at home station and deployment environments.
29957866|ab|3|29957866|AIMS|OBJECTIVE|OBJECTIVE|This integrative review examines the incidence, prevalence, and risk factors for musculoskeletal pain (MSP) and headaches in active duty (AD) military populations.
29957866|ab|4|29957866|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|Peer-reviewed research published between 2001 and 2016 was identified relevant to MSP and headache in AD military personnel using MeSH terms in key biomedical databases.
29957866|ab|5|29957866|METHODS|METHODS|METHODS|Inclusion criteria were: epidemiological studies examining MSP or headache as primary or secondary outcome; samples that included AD populations; and studies conducted in the theater of operations, at home station, and in military treatment or Veterans Health Administration facilities.
29957866|ab|6|29957866|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Twenty-six articles met inclusion criteria.
29957866|ab|7|29957866|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Low back pain (LBP) was the most prevalent MSP diagnosis.
29957866|ab|8|29957866|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|The incidence of LBP was 40.5 per 1,000 person-years and was comparable to nonmilitary populations.
29957866|ab|9|29957866|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Inflammation and pain from overuse comprised the largest proportion of injury mechanism, accounting for about 82% of all injuries among nondeployed military personnel.
29957866|ab|10|29957866|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|The risk of MSP was greater for AD, female, Army, enlisted personnel, and those with greater time in a motor vehicle.
29957866|ab|11|29957866|RESULTS|RESULTS|RESULTS|Evidence suggests posttraumatic headache, occurring in up to 92% of military personnel who have sustained a mild traumatic brain injury, is associated with chronic daily headaches.
29957866|ab|12|29957866|IMPLICATIONS|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|Nurses must recognize the consequences military service can have on the development of pain.
29957866|ab|13|29957866|IMPLICATIONS|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|Nurses have an opportunity to positively impact the health and well-being of military and veteran populations through early recognition and treatment of pain.
29957866|ab|14|29957866|IMPLICATIONS|CONCLUSIONS|CONCLUSIONS|The findings from this review underscore considerable magnitude of MSP in military personnel and expose modifiable risk factors and potential targets for designing nurse-led interventions to improve pain and symptoms in military subpopulations.
